REACT

# 

<span key="7b2d0bcc2aab4ee4ae2a78c015666824"><span offset-key="7b2d0bcc2aab4ee4ae2a78c015666824:0">Getting Started with Create React App</span></span>

<span key="b68d0175b0704e90b9519c492585b760"><span offset-key="b68d0175b0704e90b9519c492585b760:0">This project was bootstrapped with </span></span><a href="https://github.com/facebook/create-react-app" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="020745cff46f4916a17a9f2aa8a33a15" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="82e00c5131804b3da490353ffa0d346b"><span data-offset-key="82e00c5131804b3da490353ffa0d346b:0">Create React App</span></span></span></a><span key="8a70b78eba084f70ad71b16d2fa0bc75"><span offset-key="8a70b78eba084f70ad71b16d2fa0bc75:0">.</span></span>

## 

<span key="dc709bc166fe407d8b196a3b70de4afc"><span offset-key="dc709bc166fe407d8b196a3b70de4afc:0">Available Scripts</span></span>

<span key="c5a917eb50774c6a915a45be0eff31ac"><span offset-key="c5a917eb50774c6a915a45be0eff31ac:0">In the project directory, you can run:</span></span>

### 

<span key="8aeb8636b3af4118908d474fb05e2d87"><span offset-key="8aeb8636b3af4118908d474fb05e2d87:0">npm start</span></span>

<span key="4050b74683e4469ea3c6d83f00ff8f7b"><span offset-key="4050b74683e4469ea3c6d83f00ff8f7b:0">Runs the app in the development mode. Open </span></span><a href="http://localhost:3000" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="c04ab36278e14ad39ef5a6d44a9a1a7d" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="9e9be8f1ea3c4c7ca17276120f8316c1"><span data-offset-key="9e9be8f1ea3c4c7ca17276120f8316c1:0">http://localhost:3000</span></span></span></a><span key="b7a7a511fd79468b983a9c663a606e7c"><span offset-key="b7a7a511fd79468b983a9c663a606e7c:0"> to view it in your browser.</span></span>

<span key="a18e34b86b7848c6a877432619b2fa17"><span offset-key="a18e34b86b7848c6a877432619b2fa17:0">The page will reload when you make changes. You may also see any lint errors in the console.</span></span>

### 

<span key="757320be6d914bfb9232dcd65da5ad56"><span offset-key="757320be6d914bfb9232dcd65da5ad56:0">npm test</span></span>

<span key="4babd4045e2d4e4b800b0d9fa7c9333a"><span offset-key="4babd4045e2d4e4b800b0d9fa7c9333a:0">Launches the test runner in the interactive watch mode. See the section about </span></span><a href="https://facebook.github.io/create-react-app/docs/running-tests" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="59e44e83a1e24449a5f91a9e04ae8957" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="ec24a8ee3dff473a940fc0944494af90"><span data-offset-key="ec24a8ee3dff473a940fc0944494af90:0">running tests</span></span></span></a><span key="7c690adbf9db486ea87e0f90c24e9490"><span offset-key="7c690adbf9db486ea87e0f90c24e9490:0"> for more information.</span></span>

### 

<span key="68e4b8a5ba814836965cf0813f0bd0aa"><span offset-key="68e4b8a5ba814836965cf0813f0bd0aa:0">npm run build</span></span>

<span key="636a7cb8c41a45c9800d16758bbee830"><span offset-key="636a7cb8c41a45c9800d16758bbee830:0">Builds the app for production to the build folder. It correctly bundles React in production mode and optimizes the build for the best performance.</span></span>

<span key="a2e1e91006014e328ab29e1d27d14d20"><span offset-key="a2e1e91006014e328ab29e1d27d14d20:0">The build is minified and the filenames include the hashes. Your app is ready to be deployed!</span></span>

<span key="58fec4594280489d88332c1611f8f7c3"><span offset-key="58fec4594280489d88332c1611f8f7c3:0">See the section about </span></span><a href="https://facebook.github.io/create-react-app/docs/deployment" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="4f99739b9ab442ac97abb83a8f6c8be7" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="3dd0a2c5991c4566b0919ebe989962ce"><span data-offset-key="3dd0a2c5991c4566b0919ebe989962ce:0">deployment</span></span></span></a><span key="f667a9f7fbcc44449ef7411dcce9d250"><span offset-key="f667a9f7fbcc44449ef7411dcce9d250:0"> for more information.</span></span>

### 

<span key="661a639263124568a5f54438ece8fcdd"><span offset-key="661a639263124568a5f54438ece8fcdd:0">npm run eject</span></span>

<span key="cd8329e93e264284b1f1715a3c45f884">**Note: this is a one-way operation. Once you eject, you can't go back!**</span>

<span key="7f279628d755448aadea131729f9a95b"><span offset-key="7f279628d755448aadea131729f9a95b:0">If you aren't satisfied with the build tool and configuration choices, you can eject at any time. This command will remove the single build dependency from your project.</span></span>

<span key="0af18e092c4f4d3a92cf3f1ac90ec38a"><span offset-key="0af18e092c4f4d3a92cf3f1ac90ec38a:0">Instead, it will copy all the configuration files and the transitive dependencies (webpack, Babel, ESLint, etc) right into your project so you have full control over them. All of the commands except eject will still work, but they will point to the copied scripts so you can tweak them. At this point you're on your own.</span></span>

<span key="ad593d2adeef48189dbff825ed093d4d"><span offset-key="ad593d2adeef48189dbff825ed093d4d:0">You don't have to ever use eject. The curated feature set is suitable for small and middle deployments, and you shouldn't feel obligated to use this feature. However we understand that this tool wouldn't be useful if you couldn't customize it when you are ready for it.</span></span>

## 

<span key="6e438b08d1a441aaa9b333ac2f23f06c"><span offset-key="6e438b08d1a441aaa9b333ac2f23f06c:0">Learn More</span></span>

<span key="1481ddf11a93483ba7c74a3ff6c21f79"><span offset-key="1481ddf11a93483ba7c74a3ff6c21f79:0">You can learn more in the </span></span><a href="https://facebook.github.io/create-react-app/docs/getting-started" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="5c24f1841e19477aaf79b23367cadd3d" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="e2af7e9df0064c74acb8c91b488d3ab0"><span data-offset-key="e2af7e9df0064c74acb8c91b488d3ab0:0">Create React App documentation</span></span></span></a><span key="373293a2575e49ac8eb5b24106980734"><span offset-key="373293a2575e49ac8eb5b24106980734:0">.</span></span>

<span key="e6d64e098c8745ef94c8b9a812e499c0"><span offset-key="e6d64e098c8745ef94c8b9a812e499c0:0">To learn React, check out the </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="3f3e34bf3a574c2abc776e78410ddb5d" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="a3664ee11de945e18f5afc69bcc489ac"><span data-offset-key="a3664ee11de945e18f5afc69bcc489ac:0">React documentation</span></span></span></a><span key="16fcd4db2cc7481389d72be3e9a817d1"><span offset-key="16fcd4db2cc7481389d72be3e9a817d1:0">.</span></span>

### 

<span key="f348a342a50246dd8d5ca4e279db191c"><span offset-key="f348a342a50246dd8d5ca4e279db191c:0">Deployment</span></span>

<span key="f977a7826d3249f78afa389ba71e8646"><span offset-key="f977a7826d3249f78afa389ba71e8646:0">This section has moved here: </span></span><a href="https://facebook.github.io/create-react-app/docs/deployment" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="75d9ef7433234354b36f28d90f790a44" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="afadd3876cc2455c9156bd552d292cdc"><span data-offset-key="afadd3876cc2455c9156bd552d292cdc:0">https://facebook.github.io/create-react-app/docs/deployment</span></span></span></a><span key="207f4b66b61949319756923d850e8f67"><span offset-key="207f4b66b61949319756923d850e8f67:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

### 

<span key="7364b451025f430a92001acc8287810e"><span offset-key="7364b451025f430a92001acc8287810e:0">npm run build fails to minify</span></span>

<span key="ac97395571a74cbd9d48a23fca2314f1"><span offset-key="ac97395571a74cbd9d48a23fca2314f1:0">This section has moved here: </span></span><a href="https://facebook.github.io/create-react-app/docs/troubleshooting#npm-run-build-fails-to-minify" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="a3d66119938643558a2cb207b9f1749a" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="8419fdf2ab1b43549b6be58b331eec2f"><span data-offset-key="8419fdf2ab1b43549b6be58b331eec2f:0">https://facebook.github.io/create-react-app/docs/troubleshooting#npm-run-build-fails-to-minify</span></span></span></a><span key="a38c9b3b806c43c981d49e22fe372ea3"><span offset-key="a38c9b3b806c43c981d49e22fe372ea3:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

# 

<span key="643f388178e044dfae7db619a61f5041">**Hello World**</span>

# 

<span key="b1299aa1c26a4927a8e2ad3613b1dfba"><span offset-key="b1299aa1c26a4927a8e2ad3613b1dfba:0">The smallest React example looks like this:</span></span>

<span key="e0cf2e0e9083457cb241b7562f3844df"><span offset-key="e0cf2e0e9083457cb241b7562f3844df:0">It displays a heading saying "Hello, world!" on the page.</span></span>

<span key="e8959fa9a61549a2842de218aa86c7ea"><span offset-key="e8959fa9a61549a2842de218aa86c7ea:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/redirect-to-codepen/hello-world" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="dc817970cad5433c8192fb29ca599311" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="80f002e54f774c7c9a3ab3737299b3c3"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="8d172238c644425db4a743ce5959797e"><span offset-key="8d172238c644425db4a743ce5959797e:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="a00fb834bccb404ebd4e56fd665311a1"><span offset-key="a00fb834bccb404ebd4e56fd665311a1:0">Click the link above to open an online editor. Feel free to make some changes, and see how they affect the output. Most pages in this guide will have editable examples like this one.</span></span>

# 

<span key="59cc3b98204f4851bc676ea6dd7fb3bc"><span offset-key="59cc3b98204f4851bc676ea6dd7fb3bc:0">How to Read This Guide</span></span>

<span key="e600a606f3ef4b93b4be5c6c0e98f0ea"><span offset-key="e600a606f3ef4b93b4be5c6c0e98f0ea:0">In this guide, we will examine the building blocks of React apps: elements and components. Once you master them, you can create complex apps from small reusable pieces.</span></span>

> <span key="c45667d2fbef4f63a2574271529c18eb"><span offset-key="c45667d2fbef4f63a2574271529c18eb:0">TipThis guide is designed for people who prefer learning concepts step by step. If you prefer to learn by doing, check out our practical tutorial. You might find this guide and the tutorial complementary to each other.</span></span>

<span key="a3ef08ee7a4e40c4843081f608bfdc69"><span offset-key="a3ef08ee7a4e40c4843081f608bfdc69:0">This is the first chapter in a step-by-step guide about main React concepts. You can find a list of all its chapters in the navigation sidebar. If you're reading this from a mobile device, you can access the navigation by pressing the button in the bottom right corner of your screen.</span></span>

<span key="f24487867ec0423ebe4511a16a9522c8"><span offset-key="f24487867ec0423ebe4511a16a9522c8:0">Every chapter in this guide builds on the knowledge introduced in earlier chapters. </span>**You can learn most of React by reading the "Main Concepts" guide chapters in the order they appear in the sidebar.**<span offset-key="f24487867ec0423ebe4511a16a9522c8:2"> For example, </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/introducing-jsx.html" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="97e7e230c6e2405897dbbc6df6b827d6" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="76f08464bcea47be92e1ae842d976b2f"><span data-offset-key="76f08464bcea47be92e1ae842d976b2f:0">"Introducing JSX"</span></span></span></a><span key="005b73db6b134bef8d965350a1a9d519"><span offset-key="005b73db6b134bef8d965350a1a9d519:0"> is the next chapter after this one.</span></span>

# 

<span key="66b4393e7a394a419a45a31603e7459e"><span offset-key="66b4393e7a394a419a45a31603e7459e:0">Knowledge Level Assumptions</span></span>

<span key="4d2630b360a24e11a216b79715e4b63b"><span offset-key="4d2630b360a24e11a216b79715e4b63b:0">React is a JavaScript library, and so we'll assume you have a basic understanding of the JavaScript language. </span>**If you don't feel very confident, we recommend**<span offset-key="4d2630b360a24e11a216b79715e4b63b:2"> </span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/A_re-introduction_to_JavaScript" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="7964eec661934a63809b1b9b3b28dc33" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="3fcd19bb6b5c46a8bbf9b59b4e61869c"><strong>going through a JavaScript tutorial</strong></span></span></a><span key="c75c0d280d5b446fbe12bc78e2ce0b2f"><span offset-key="c75c0d280d5b446fbe12bc78e2ce0b2f:0"> to check your knowledge level and enable you to follow along this guide without getting lost. It might take you between 30 minutes and an hour, but as a result you won't have to feel like you're learning both React and JavaScript at the same time.</span></span>

> <span key="0d8c61a11b4342f6aa5e914c986d0013"><span offset-key="0d8c61a11b4342f6aa5e914c986d0013:0">NoteThis guide occasionally uses some newer JavaScript syntax in the examples. If you haven't worked with JavaScript in the last few years, these three points should get you most of the way.</span></span>

# 

<span key="9e4b74a1dd8e473dbda4cee9b26dd916">**Introducing JSX**</span>

# 

<span key="c258afc622f5400c9967f05e381c750a"><span offset-key="c258afc622f5400c9967f05e381c750a:0">Consider this variable declaration:</span></span>

<span key="27f73ea6c52e420eb2b562eaf3f08b59"><span offset-key="27f73ea6c52e420eb2b562eaf3f08b59:0">This funny tag syntax is neither a string nor HTML.</span></span>

<span key="2be4beb7aff7469596f9b7cc4621fb6a"><span offset-key="2be4beb7aff7469596f9b7cc4621fb6a:0">It is called JSX, and it is a syntax extension to JavaScript. We recommend using it with React to describe what the UI should look like. JSX may remind you of a template language, but it comes with the full power of JavaScript.</span></span>

<span key="d3d3549f4ade4a5ebe63e35f4750712a"><span offset-key="d3d3549f4ade4a5ebe63e35f4750712a:0">JSX produces React "elements". We will explore rendering them to the DOM in the </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/rendering-elements.html" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="2da24819ac624c4cb261d9c2a2178e6c" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="be429c7150df493e93911f0fff03760a"><span data-offset-key="be429c7150df493e93911f0fff03760a:0">next section</span></span></span></a><span key="0cc1cfcd058f483e835bfbc565f880df"><span offset-key="0cc1cfcd058f483e835bfbc565f880df:0">. Below, you can find the basics of JSX necessary to get you started.</span></span>

# 

<span key="c4478ccf3a574ad78ca332ceb85848c2"><span offset-key="c4478ccf3a574ad78ca332ceb85848c2:0">Why JSX?</span></span>

<span key="fe0018724f4b486dbbf928d1526156ce"><span offset-key="fe0018724f4b486dbbf928d1526156ce:0">React embraces the fact that rendering logic is inherently coupled with other UI logic: how events are handled, how the state changes over time, and how the data is prepared for display.</span></span>

<span key="7ceaab0a15f448818ef73847f86ed6dd"><span offset-key="7ceaab0a15f448818ef73847f86ed6dd:0">Instead of artificially separating </span>*technologies*<span offset-key="7ceaab0a15f448818ef73847f86ed6dd:2"> by putting markup and logic in separate files, React </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Separation_of_concerns" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="8ef55e0928594fa590bd284f976d21a6" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="72c3589c28784c1e87b00f898d097446"><span data-offset-key="72c3589c28784c1e87b00f898d097446:0">separates </span><em>concerns</em></span></span></a><span key="5ff15c7fa4e84f7eb81552a50b25a841"><span offset-key="5ff15c7fa4e84f7eb81552a50b25a841:0"> with loosely coupled units called "components" that contain both. We will come back to components in a </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/components-and-props.html" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="852dc7f9bc2d4bb18ae723ed3e94a41d" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="84de41dcd3514f4fa17ae279195527f6"><span data-offset-key="84de41dcd3514f4fa17ae279195527f6:0">further section</span></span></span></a><span key="1ad149b897eb4175a810e74e4067578d"><span offset-key="1ad149b897eb4175a810e74e4067578d:0">, but if you're not yet comfortable putting markup in JS, </span></span><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=x7cQ3mrcKaY" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="6060d97136004a72aef9a7d137e92f20" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="85765b7041134f8cbaec924175b5dcd0"><span data-offset-key="85765b7041134f8cbaec924175b5dcd0:0">this talk</span></span></span></a><span key="9523be7dc7ac4a3c8ebf306b48e3bb18"><span offset-key="9523be7dc7ac4a3c8ebf306b48e3bb18:0"> might convince you otherwise.</span></span>

<span key="57009aaaf02f4db29e834beba17769fd"><span offset-key="57009aaaf02f4db29e834beba17769fd:0">React </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/react-without-jsx.html" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="8f460d0f66014b09904b0a0c8de58f8b" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="668a5ac68d4049d39f2f86a665aff1f5"><span data-offset-key="668a5ac68d4049d39f2f86a665aff1f5:0">doesn't require</span></span></span></a><span key="23abe39fd62848a7883545168103b682"><span offset-key="23abe39fd62848a7883545168103b682:0"> using JSX, but most people find it helpful as a visual aid when working with UI inside the JavaScript code. It also allows React to show more useful error and warning messages.</span></span>

<span key="00583d4adbdc4816bb8d8d6cb6fa07ab"><span offset-key="00583d4adbdc4816bb8d8d6cb6fa07ab:0">With that out of the way, let's get started!</span></span>

# 

<span key="18062e381217498d88a55b1f13a04c50"><span offset-key="18062e381217498d88a55b1f13a04c50:0">Embedding Expressions in JSX</span></span>

<span key="76aa07e7b32149f9b5a978757de25ed2"><span offset-key="76aa07e7b32149f9b5a978757de25ed2:0">In the example below, we declare a variable called name and then use it inside JSX by wrapping it in curly braces:</span></span>

<span key="28d3d67b19a846fdb147219a7b9955fb"><span offset-key="28d3d67b19a846fdb147219a7b9955fb:0">You can put any valid </span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Guide/Expressions_and_Operators#Expressions" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="027165cf65784493b8df9ff1367d4ddf" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="35b802cba879422688e4486cfbcba5b7"><span data-offset-key="35b802cba879422688e4486cfbcba5b7:0">JavaScript expression</span></span></span></a><span key="22737659b79147feb93818aacdb2f889"><span offset-key="22737659b79147feb93818aacdb2f889:0"> inside the curly braces in JSX. For example, 2 + 2, user.firstName, or formatName(user) are all valid JavaScript expressions.</span></span>

<span key="3dff1da3c6a64fd0b3c68e8065bcc90a"><span offset-key="3dff1da3c6a64fd0b3c68e8065bcc90a:0">In the example below, we embed the result of calling a JavaScript function, formatName(user), into an &lt;h1> element.</span></span>

<span key="e49a934ea2ae48219bdeb2739b53082f"><span offset-key="e49a934ea2ae48219bdeb2739b53082f:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/redirect-to-codepen/introducing-jsx" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="1c375beae5fb442a8e68a5d0ad418f80" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="9433680874024781b581b65d2d5842d2"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="505f5782277f4250bd6fa37113e7eb77"><span offset-key="505f5782277f4250bd6fa37113e7eb77:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="1f24030a57134a2790bf78a74e416f99"><span offset-key="1f24030a57134a2790bf78a74e416f99:0">We split JSX over multiple lines for readability. While it isn't required, when doing this, we also recommend wrapping it in parentheses to avoid the pitfalls of </span></span><a href="https://stackoverflow.com/q/2846283" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="daacdc22579642a3bf2ce9063ee53c05" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="da1d0af9f700469fbc59562a69e30206"><span data-offset-key="da1d0af9f700469fbc59562a69e30206:0">automatic semicolon insertion</span></span></span></a><span key="c0b0df8b5d9d4e4ebf1875f5bf03b2b2"><span offset-key="c0b0df8b5d9d4e4ebf1875f5bf03b2b2:0">.</span></span>

# 

<span key="ee442cdf88374a159f9f6ab26769a47b"><span offset-key="ee442cdf88374a159f9f6ab26769a47b:0">JSX is an Expression Too</span></span>

<span key="a68365c26b234b2b8dda71871069676c"><span offset-key="a68365c26b234b2b8dda71871069676c:0">After compilation, JSX expressions become regular JavaScript function calls and evaluate to JavaScript objects.</span></span>

<span key="dda2acc7853b4981a91321baca9685e6"><span offset-key="dda2acc7853b4981a91321baca9685e6:0">This means that you can use JSX inside of if statements and for loops, assign it to variables, accept it as arguments, and return it from functions:</span></span>

# 

<span key="17003c4d9fc746feb2eec42023c36f46"><span offset-key="17003c4d9fc746feb2eec42023c36f46:0">Specifying Attributes with JSX</span></span>

<span key="fc8c4904a7644c9db5640d937d7b7c2a"><span offset-key="fc8c4904a7644c9db5640d937d7b7c2a:0">You may use quotes to specify string literals as attributes:</span></span>

<span key="40b7fe49f89241bca26e434186651578"><span offset-key="40b7fe49f89241bca26e434186651578:0">You may also use curly braces to embed a JavaScript expression in an attribute:</span></span>

<span key="a63505428f0842d6859bfd38e7d94882"><span offset-key="a63505428f0842d6859bfd38e7d94882:0">Don't put quotes around curly braces when embedding a JavaScript expression in an attribute. You should either use quotes (for string values) or curly braces (for expressions), but not both in the same attribute.</span></span>

> <span key="b170c39a88174afcbef0bf227845b8d8"><span offset-key="b170c39a88174afcbef0bf227845b8d8:0">Warning:Since JSX is closer to JavaScript than to HTML, React DOM uses camelCase property naming convention instead of HTML attribute names.For example, class becomes className in JSX, and tabindex becomes tabIndex.</span></span>

# 

<span key="f3166ae3b8594e4abac4f4df24e66053"><span offset-key="f3166ae3b8594e4abac4f4df24e66053:0">Specifying Children with JSX</span></span>

<span key="3ff7c0812e0a4135ba2c9a5f7f727333"><span offset-key="3ff7c0812e0a4135ba2c9a5f7f727333:0">If a tag is empty, you may close it immediately with />, like XML:</span></span>

<span key="928a42a6900440688b87ea586bf4e728"><span offset-key="928a42a6900440688b87ea586bf4e728:0">JSX tags may contain children:</span></span>

# 

<span key="9f0b70091505476c89aee65ea86b7b4e"><span offset-key="9f0b70091505476c89aee65ea86b7b4e:0">JSX Prevents Injection Attacks</span></span>

<span key="3d2ffd40b60c409b9a28d628097adce4"><span offset-key="3d2ffd40b60c409b9a28d628097adce4:0">It is safe to embed user input in JSX:</span></span>

<span key="3897a59b98ee465c9f92ef0576abb6ad"><span offset-key="3897a59b98ee465c9f92ef0576abb6ad:0">By default, React DOM </span></span><a href="https://stackoverflow.com/questions/7381974/which-characters-need-to-be-escaped-on-html" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="4097bc26c6ec475b9055c8e353c62896" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="f1fb348e29ed4625b03d369e232642d0"><span data-offset-key="f1fb348e29ed4625b03d369e232642d0:0">escapes</span></span></span></a><span key="ff4b88308321405891dc73470751019c"><span offset-key="ff4b88308321405891dc73470751019c:0"> any values embedded in JSX before rendering them. Thus it ensures that you can never inject anything that's not explicitly written in your application. Everything is converted to a string before being rendered. This helps prevent </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cross-site_scripting" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="987bc020838b486c8c2f305ced51e8da" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="c27d8025884943d79c6c7af5bbc5ece7"><span data-offset-key="c27d8025884943d79c6c7af5bbc5ece7:0">XSS (cross-site-scripting)</span></span></span></a><span key="dc64aca4a16445119da9b7a76c5c48ec"><span offset-key="dc64aca4a16445119da9b7a76c5c48ec:0"> attacks.</span></span>

# 

<span key="28471397fac4474db3539959474b2b16"><span offset-key="28471397fac4474db3539959474b2b16:0">JSX Represents Objects</span></span>

<span key="16bba2f546154949bb5f1360dcca65c7"><span offset-key="16bba2f546154949bb5f1360dcca65c7:0">Babel compiles JSX down to React.createElement() calls.</span></span>

<span key="97587efabc004d0fac0f960342ba5813"><span offset-key="97587efabc004d0fac0f960342ba5813:0">These two examples are identical:</span></span>

<span key="7e59542205f94e7d89d9e2e0fa81dead"><span offset-key="7e59542205f94e7d89d9e2e0fa81dead:0">React.createElement() performs a few checks to help you write bug-free code but essentially it creates an object like this:</span></span>

<span key="5dc7931566604aa2a69b51a6ab595bc8"><span offset-key="5dc7931566604aa2a69b51a6ab595bc8:0">These objects are called "React elements". You can think of them as descriptions of what you want to see on the screen. React reads these objects and uses them to construct the DOM and keep it up to date.</span></span>

<span key="1aae6f0240044676b4c6d4ad2758a730"><span offset-key="1aae6f0240044676b4c6d4ad2758a730:0">We will explore rendering React elements to the DOM in the </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/rendering-elements.html" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="a88b935aa0d141a0b9e7676122486388" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="7d1c7d64361a4953967f849da253569b"><span data-offset-key="7d1c7d64361a4953967f849da253569b:0">next section</span></span></span></a><span key="b8759f67869042469069b391a420f529"><span offset-key="b8759f67869042469069b391a420f529:0">.</span></span>

> <span key="2a3482d40b3747d9bce295742c008296"><span offset-key="2a3482d40b3747d9bce295742c008296:0">Tip:We recommend using the "Babel" language definition for your editor of choice so that both ES6 and JSX code is properly highlighted.</span></span>

# 

<span key="b40db7d4741e46108c3e1ef828987d13">**Rendering Elements**</span>

# 

<span key="750708d7d611402297c34c0322ccd321"><span offset-key="750708d7d611402297c34c0322ccd321:0">Elements are the smallest building blocks of React apps.</span></span>

<span key="72f533085fba484cbd859a14bd556707"><span offset-key="72f533085fba484cbd859a14bd556707:0">An element describes what you want to see on the screen:</span></span>

<span key="45071e63eabb4c09b81f2ee4b83255b8"><span offset-key="45071e63eabb4c09b81f2ee4b83255b8:0">const element = &lt;h1>Hello, world&lt;/h1>;</span></span>

<span key="f0a2500edf704bb19b77a6c468c9b20d"><span offset-key="f0a2500edf704bb19b77a6c468c9b20d:0">Unlike browser DOM elements, React elements are plain objects, and are cheap to create. React DOM takes care of updating the DOM to match the React elements.</span></span>

> <span key="426b3f023ff44ec48da9f35f3faa5797"><span offset-key="426b3f023ff44ec48da9f35f3faa5797:0">Note:One might confuse elements with a more widely known concept of "components". We will introduce components in the next section. Elements are what components are "made of", and we encourage you to read this section before jumping ahead.</span></span>

# 

<span key="dfa5956d62f0446ebe78aef450e8a3b2"><span offset-key="dfa5956d62f0446ebe78aef450e8a3b2:0">Rendering an Element into the DOM</span></span>

<span key="d5ad85cc80d24c01ac35b07d59be6c7a"><span offset-key="d5ad85cc80d24c01ac35b07d59be6c7a:0">Let's say there is a &lt;div> somewhere in your HTML file:</span></span>

<span key="b43e9ccf118c45fb9c8b65cf5e30229f"><span offset-key="b43e9ccf118c45fb9c8b65cf5e30229f:0">We call this a "root" DOM node because everything inside it will be managed by React DOM.</span></span>

<span key="f01396e992fe4502b3e6705d968cdbe5"><span offset-key="f01396e992fe4502b3e6705d968cdbe5:0">Applications built with just React usually have a single root DOM node. If you are integrating React into an existing app, you may have as many isolated root DOM nodes as you like.</span></span>

<span key="957275accada4f2981a4be8b0f71e2df"><span offset-key="957275accada4f2981a4be8b0f71e2df:0">To render a React element into a root DOM node, pass both to \[ReactDOM.render()\](&lt;</span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/react-dom.html#render%3E" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="e96d7e7ecc95461a8b05945e0bb5ef0d" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="4c61ac00400f4e43943be470cdc22788"><span data-offset-key="4c61ac00400f4e43943be470cdc22788:0">https://reactjs.org/docs/react-dom.html#render&gt;</span></span></span></a><span key="8e5dbd2709bf4259b38c8e6d0d663804"><span offset-key="8e5dbd2709bf4259b38c8e6d0d663804:0">):</span></span>

<span key="9991115150ca401f9e490230d9c2d06a"><span offset-key="9991115150ca401f9e490230d9c2d06a:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/redirect-to-codepen/rendering-elements/render-an-element" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="c87fbdf909c145ba9d02a4534852fd6d" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="770ddaa790a640afbbfa6f9bd70a5cec"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="54224ec7bb284db4b53fc1642f66dd1b"><span offset-key="54224ec7bb284db4b53fc1642f66dd1b:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="c061ca5af9864d63ba2e54955bbf24a6"><span offset-key="c061ca5af9864d63ba2e54955bbf24a6:0">It displays "Hello, world" on the page.</span></span>

# 

<span key="21bbe50c3d72463eb1873eb5eb3750fa"><span offset-key="21bbe50c3d72463eb1873eb5eb3750fa:0">Updating the Rendered Element</span></span>

<span key="d6a82608d90b432b80b1c57d3a05d5d7"><span offset-key="d6a82608d90b432b80b1c57d3a05d5d7:0">React elements are </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immutable_object" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="680e248760f945929fc84a8c5bf6cc5d" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="4de077d5d0c943bc8c258d8ba2dbf652"><span data-offset-key="4de077d5d0c943bc8c258d8ba2dbf652:0">immutable</span></span></span></a><span key="e6bf3a2c04c945baaec03fb6c3ab59ac"><span offset-key="e6bf3a2c04c945baaec03fb6c3ab59ac:0">. Once you create an element, you can't change its children or attributes. An element is like a single frame in a movie: it represents the UI at a certain point in time.</span></span>

<span key="0c2403c401f74b7aae4f28cdbe7ca74d"><span offset-key="0c2403c401f74b7aae4f28cdbe7ca74d:0">With our knowledge so far, the only way to update the UI is to create a new element, and pass it to \[ReactDOM.render()\](&lt;</span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/react-dom.html#render%3E" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="38108815ec574b308615d203d8f95e6e" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="31c67f8a1e924e5396fd3ef1e62d7b9c"><span data-offset-key="31c67f8a1e924e5396fd3ef1e62d7b9c:0">https://reactjs.org/docs/react-dom.html#render&gt;</span></span></span></a><span key="9d225e178d7d4f88a5c56aa45278bb8d"><span offset-key="9d225e178d7d4f88a5c56aa45278bb8d:0">).</span></span>

<span key="8aacde11ea7f4bd0814500e7a224ff18"><span offset-key="8aacde11ea7f4bd0814500e7a224ff18:0">Consider this ticking clock example:</span></span>

<span key="ca22be7c24ec4dadb6e2c9782f09b881"><span offset-key="ca22be7c24ec4dadb6e2c9782f09b881:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/redirect-to-codepen/rendering-elements/update-rendered-element" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="74e499dfede54a1aa184c79e71804649" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="8c7eb6f58aa8428e916681c2ec3aeebe"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="2b4e314b716a42e4899c96e7ebf1a4c1"><span offset-key="2b4e314b716a42e4899c96e7ebf1a4c1:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="1871d833ba5a42b992ce76551a41d300"><span offset-key="1871d833ba5a42b992ce76551a41d300:0">It calls \[ReactDOM.render()\](&lt;</span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/react-dom.html#render%3E" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="024c4636dd3740a0891167c69a1dba15" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="92319d4fb7fa49ee8c67fc97802482aa"><span data-offset-key="92319d4fb7fa49ee8c67fc97802482aa:0">https://reactjs.org/docs/react-dom.html#render&gt;</span></span></span></a><span key="70394265bfb94fbba79c86ac7449fcc8"><span offset-key="70394265bfb94fbba79c86ac7449fcc8:0">) every second from a \[setInterval()\](&lt;</span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/WindowTimers/setInterval%3E" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="a33d877ff026464db2d2b4099b0df16c" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="a342f0d1e2444eea8a75973f217bd483"><span data-offset-key="a342f0d1e2444eea8a75973f217bd483:0">https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/WindowTimers/setInterval&gt;</span></span></span></a><span key="8b2032317bf040ddbddefc30a7dd437d"><span offset-key="8b2032317bf040ddbddefc30a7dd437d:0">) callback.</span></span>

> <span key="cb2349c4395e4682959c6ff030fb79c4"><span offset-key="cb2349c4395e4682959c6ff030fb79c4:0">Note:In practice, most React apps only call ReactDOM.render() once. In the next sections we will learn how such code gets encapsulated into stateful components.We recommend that you don't skip topics because they build on each other.</span></span>

# 

<span key="5268bbfd1c6646548242de15d9ebd692"><span offset-key="5268bbfd1c6646548242de15d9ebd692:0">React Only Updates What's Necessary</span></span>

<span key="e1090a642c324e4d8eef6374fd806a6d"><span offset-key="e1090a642c324e4d8eef6374fd806a6d:0">React DOM compares the element and its children to the previous one, and only applies the DOM updates necessary to bring the DOM to the desired state.</span></span>

<span key="6e2792b4d740439e962611f7d710f9ce"><span offset-key="6e2792b4d740439e962611f7d710f9ce:0">You can verify by inspecting the </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/redirect-to-codepen/rendering-elements/update-rendered-element" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="159dced861194cfd95e04220962db77f" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="ec2974a0fc8142109eed0e4ed59fa164"><span data-offset-key="ec2974a0fc8142109eed0e4ed59fa164:0">last example</span></span></span></a><span key="cfe86c0f8f8a4b13946edeb17d96f570"><span offset-key="cfe86c0f8f8a4b13946edeb17d96f570:0"> with the browser tools:</span></span>

<span key="b86197dcf45641818decb39cadbece56"><span offset-key="b86197dcf45641818decb39cadbece56:0">Even though we create an element describing the whole UI tree on every tick, only the text node whose contents have changed gets updated by React DOM.</span></span>

<span key="e8af373dc95f4f5eb8150a6338c8ecc2"><span offset-key="e8af373dc95f4f5eb8150a6338c8ecc2:0">In our experience, thinking about how the UI should look at any given moment, rather than how to change it over time, eliminates a whole class of bugs.</span></span>

# 

<span key="be705165526246f18fec5c6a1d411628">**Components and Props**</span>

# 

<span key="1080c003f6bb461cb641efdc28c92b52"><span offset-key="1080c003f6bb461cb641efdc28c92b52:0">Components let you split the UI into independent, reusable pieces, and think about each piece in isolation. This page provides an introduction to the idea of components. You can find a </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/react-component.html" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="2328a6a9e8714dc5b9a3a0cd88bb88db" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="a6c73fec955c4d6dae6a103ef24d1a0c"><span data-offset-key="a6c73fec955c4d6dae6a103ef24d1a0c:0">detailed component API reference here</span></span></span></a><span key="34cec80996ed45b3b595e4572c42a75a"><span offset-key="34cec80996ed45b3b595e4572c42a75a:0">.</span></span>

<span key="05e320604c4d474f8b40b7700a2e28cb"><span offset-key="05e320604c4d474f8b40b7700a2e28cb:0">Conceptually, components are like JavaScript functions. They accept arbitrary inputs (called "props") and return React elements describing what should appear on the screen.</span></span>

# 

<span key="174a722688ab491e9b30d40cc83caa2a"><span offset-key="174a722688ab491e9b30d40cc83caa2a:0">Function and Class Components</span></span>

<span key="074c7503aa884850824ca6e31b0bb4b3"><span offset-key="074c7503aa884850824ca6e31b0bb4b3:0">The simplest way to define a component is to write a JavaScript function:</span></span>

<span key="c0c2c0148b694997a7d4c524a9e400f2"><span offset-key="c0c2c0148b694997a7d4c524a9e400f2:0">This function is a valid React component because it accepts a single "props" (which stands for properties) object argument with data and returns a React element. We call such components "function components" because they are literally JavaScript functions.</span></span>

<span key="cc5191eb3a37465d95d148f489b6361e"><span offset-key="cc5191eb3a37465d95d148f489b6361e:0">You can also use an </span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Classes" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="c233dc4a604a473088cdc78dfd0a1d76" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="fb7b87ce9a594ab6b66fd8029a222631"><span data-offset-key="fb7b87ce9a594ab6b66fd8029a222631:0">ES6 class</span></span></span></a><span key="8324ff4fa22d4c7288f7439f865f6593"><span offset-key="8324ff4fa22d4c7288f7439f865f6593:0"> to define a component:</span></span>

<span key="2ff1071489aa497199fec15efa967728"><span offset-key="2ff1071489aa497199fec15efa967728:0">The above two components are equivalent from React's point of view.</span></span>

<span key="9789332e536b4f6385700f81c7c1ee3a"><span offset-key="9789332e536b4f6385700f81c7c1ee3a:0">Function and Class components both have some additional features that we will discuss in the </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/state-and-lifecycle.html" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="f8877f7793204441b87b7b6923a3ee85" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="1b2292bc49d1471bb6e7d3be5e1a266a"><span data-offset-key="1b2292bc49d1471bb6e7d3be5e1a266a:0">next sections</span></span></span></a><span key="1b893fac662d400e970a8be706e4e1b0"><span offset-key="1b893fac662d400e970a8be706e4e1b0:0">.</span></span>

# 

<span key="cc2f35a1bd0a444eba4aea603ec99080"><span offset-key="cc2f35a1bd0a444eba4aea603ec99080:0">Rendering a Component</span></span>

<span key="eb1f661e824d4f5095601fbb4e30e3b8"><span offset-key="eb1f661e824d4f5095601fbb4e30e3b8:0">Previously, we only encountered React elements that represent DOM tags:</span></span>

<span key="3a1e67ce5e214c819a572e17a6c8f2f1"><span offset-key="3a1e67ce5e214c819a572e17a6c8f2f1:0">However, elements can also represent user-defined components:</span></span>

<span key="f7b571d81e05481ebdbfd68a1bf9c630"><span offset-key="f7b571d81e05481ebdbfd68a1bf9c630:0">When React sees an element representing a user-defined component, it passes JSX attributes and children to this component as a single object. We call this object "props".</span></span>

<span key="b8911bf45f584deba2ca3628e52666f1"><span offset-key="b8911bf45f584deba2ca3628e52666f1:0">For example, this code renders "Hello, Sara" on the page:</span></span>

<span key="78210942b66f408eb9c9e3251b799681"><span offset-key="78210942b66f408eb9c9e3251b799681:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/redirect-to-codepen/components-and-props/rendering-a-component" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="87bb45aa896d4f169e6869967b224a13" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="7fee7e7547074f35bf09da3111d31b8a"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="ed8e8e2ef4db43599deda5e6288bc2ac"><span offset-key="ed8e8e2ef4db43599deda5e6288bc2ac:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="758b8a56b9fd488f81858236ad9a9453"><span offset-key="758b8a56b9fd488f81858236ad9a9453:0">Let's recap what happens in this example:</span></span>

1.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">1.</span>
    <span key="c36afc4f07b54e38b975ab85a5b44c38"><span offset-key="c36afc4f07b54e38b975ab85a5b44c38:0">We call ReactDOM.render() with the &lt;Welcome name="Sara" /> element.</span></span>

2.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">2.</span>
    <span key="e2cedab62f3d43caaba1c73df6f9faf1"><span offset-key="e2cedab62f3d43caaba1c73df6f9faf1:0">React calls the Welcome component with {name: 'Sara'} as the props.</span></span>

3.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">3.</span>
    <span key="3d67719f7bcc4d398155f97b6ef6f500"><span offset-key="3d67719f7bcc4d398155f97b6ef6f500:0">Our Welcome component returns a &lt;h1>Hello, Sara&lt;/h1> element as the result.</span></span>

4.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">4.</span>
    <span key="b1a96fa4e60a46409166ee947f4dc15a"><span offset-key="b1a96fa4e60a46409166ee947f4dc15a:0">React DOM efficiently updates the DOM to match &lt;h1>Hello, Sara&lt;/h1>.</span></span>

> <span key="d592751178df4a7f8cab7fb056718e34"><span offset-key="d592751178df4a7f8cab7fb056718e34:0">Note: Always start component names with a capital letter.React treats components starting with lowercase letters as DOM tags. For example,</span></span>

# 

<span key="a4c15a5e7408492d9a975c6eab7360ca"><span offset-key="a4c15a5e7408492d9a975c6eab7360ca:0">Composing Components</span></span>

<span key="10e13a07d8b5472aa14c0c8c89706eb6"><span offset-key="10e13a07d8b5472aa14c0c8c89706eb6:0">Components can refer to other components in their output. This lets us use the same component abstraction for any level of detail. A button, a form, a dialog, a screen: in React apps, all those are commonly expressed as components.</span></span>

<span key="c88047cdc6744a40af45239b3da902f3"><span offset-key="c88047cdc6744a40af45239b3da902f3:0">For example, we can create an App component that renders Welcome many times:</span></span>

<span key="d459760797744679b0d2a65f271a32b2"><span offset-key="d459760797744679b0d2a65f271a32b2:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/redirect-to-codepen/components-and-props/composing-components" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="4c3d5496090f4c8699d010ee8e4c183e" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="57f2744c316b4d9194c8bfb946113d72"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="1b5565da2aa9460085e552f0a3f3003c"><span offset-key="1b5565da2aa9460085e552f0a3f3003c:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="a68e5046cb7c43d7afa9ce018510c8a6"><span offset-key="a68e5046cb7c43d7afa9ce018510c8a6:0">Typically, new React apps have a single App component at the very top. However, if you integrate React into an existing app, you might start bottom-up with a small component like Button and gradually work your way to the top of the view hierarchy.</span></span>

# 

<span key="b9de9a4b9f774485aed728e9c8947486"><span offset-key="b9de9a4b9f774485aed728e9c8947486:0">Extracting Components</span></span>

<span key="57e112443ac644d78f3840ef1553d158"><span offset-key="57e112443ac644d78f3840ef1553d158:0">Don't be afraid to split components into smaller components.</span></span>

<span key="3e71fd04720e4cd889a41faa47817cf0"><span offset-key="3e71fd04720e4cd889a41faa47817cf0:0">For example, consider this Comment component:</span></span>

<span key="d043378e2b964babb2a100499b0627d5"><span offset-key="d043378e2b964babb2a100499b0627d5:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/redirect-to-codepen/components-and-props/extracting-components" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="6e6b8fd1f38942e791f20ca58e9c7a63" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="725473d66e3449faa7df9cd794df94ed"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="9ee6468c2ba04b17ac12516100952e61"><span offset-key="9ee6468c2ba04b17ac12516100952e61:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="9be50e6511f34b48ae3dc1e4856e3390"><span offset-key="9be50e6511f34b48ae3dc1e4856e3390:0">It accepts author (an object), text (a string), and date (a date) as props, and describes a comment on a social media website.</span></span>

<span key="e5c7ae51169e4b37aa1663354298a269"><span offset-key="e5c7ae51169e4b37aa1663354298a269:0">This component can be tricky to change because of all the nesting, and it is also hard to reuse individual parts of it. Let's extract a few components from it.</span></span>

<span key="1b1a7d86a5f4439b96f4caef53da4ab1"><span offset-key="1b1a7d86a5f4439b96f4caef53da4ab1:0">First, we will extract Avatar:</span></span>

<span key="d50253bdca7f4505b5ca60cb2d01aae1"><span offset-key="d50253bdca7f4505b5ca60cb2d01aae1:0">The Avatar doesn't need to know that it is being rendered inside a Comment. This is why we have given its prop a more generic name: user rather than author.</span></span>

<span key="a2de0e1599684493a76f251462b95f06"><span offset-key="a2de0e1599684493a76f251462b95f06:0">We recommend naming props from the component's own point of view rather than the context in which it is being used.</span></span>

<span key="23d5de46aa1246f68baedb3713f9c561"><span offset-key="23d5de46aa1246f68baedb3713f9c561:0">We can now simplify Comment a tiny bit:</span></span>

<span key="f8e363a234ce42b8bb53db19260f89f4"><span offset-key="f8e363a234ce42b8bb53db19260f89f4:0">Next, we will extract a UserInfo component that renders an Avatar next to the user's name:</span></span>

<span key="17f233b3aa3343c7a1e90b697608a8b3"><span offset-key="17f233b3aa3343c7a1e90b697608a8b3:0">function UserInfo(props) { return ( &lt;div className="UserInfo"> &lt;Avatar user={props.user} /> &lt;div className="UserInfo-name"> {props.user.name} &lt;/div> &lt;/div> ); }</span></span>

<span key="976fbf150f8f4d9a9435a235626d8813"><span offset-key="976fbf150f8f4d9a9435a235626d8813:0">This lets us simplify Comment even further:</span></span>

<span key="d320722c691e4a89828ecf5abf80ece4"><span offset-key="d320722c691e4a89828ecf5abf80ece4:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/redirect-to-codepen/components-and-props/extracting-components-continued" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="79225476095f4b9a8f88462d1e819b56" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="4e3a41da91924481873e7820996a93fb"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="76c10909492b47f688822c1053e487ba"><span offset-key="76c10909492b47f688822c1053e487ba:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="84e3ca251a6d4aec9faee0b126636356"><span offset-key="84e3ca251a6d4aec9faee0b126636356:0">Extracting components might seem like grunt work at first, but having a palette of reusable components pays off in larger apps. A good rule of thumb is that if a part of your UI is used several times (Button, Panel, Avatar), or is complex enough on its own (App, FeedStory, Comment), it is a good candidate to be extracted to a separate component.</span></span>

# 

<span key="973dd9df477b44169705d47e7936b50d"><span offset-key="973dd9df477b44169705d47e7936b50d:0">Props are Read-Only</span></span>

<span key="305df2f5d3c740178c5fff673508330d"><span offset-key="305df2f5d3c740178c5fff673508330d:0">Whether you declare a component </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/components-and-props.html#function-and-class-components" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="f494b884a1e848c99ebd9ab8427a64a5" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="43c561b013d84183a618d87ffed0f83c"><span data-offset-key="43c561b013d84183a618d87ffed0f83c:0">as a function or a class</span></span></span></a><span key="a0c3722ab9fd4ddb837f6f2d4ab6c858"><span offset-key="a0c3722ab9fd4ddb837f6f2d4ab6c858:0">, it must never modify its own props. Consider this sum function:</span></span>

<span key="3e97068090d946e68177a9bc56a26afc"><span offset-key="3e97068090d946e68177a9bc56a26afc:0">Such functions are called </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pure_function" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="b7e02e0c5b674aada92283a1f92815a2" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="3363004c1eb34052970f811deeb1da62"><span data-offset-key="3363004c1eb34052970f811deeb1da62:0">"pure"</span></span></span></a><span key="c812fc46dcda4b42866e821969745001"><span offset-key="c812fc46dcda4b42866e821969745001:0"> because they do not attempt to change their inputs, and always return the same result for the same inputs.</span></span>

<span key="6645ff01493f4ae6a02017e8c2f63253"><span offset-key="6645ff01493f4ae6a02017e8c2f63253:0">In contrast, this function is impure because it changes its own input:</span></span>

<span key="8de7c2d99341480082e2635f96abb657"><span offset-key="8de7c2d99341480082e2635f96abb657:0">React is pretty flexible but it has a single strict rule:</span></span>

<span key="a6a89fd5a0db42ac97f2f6208e397fc8">**All React components must act like pure functions with respect to their props.**</span>

<span key="c903f7ca854d46518dfc133155f4a9a4"><span offset-key="c903f7ca854d46518dfc133155f4a9a4:0">Of course, application UIs are dynamic and change over time. In the </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/state-and-lifecycle.html" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="c2d1e5ddcace47358526528bb9c974ed" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="20742b3fc1a445509393c4831233479c"><span data-offset-key="20742b3fc1a445509393c4831233479c:0">next section</span></span></span></a><span key="d5a887c4672b42c885de063ec6aa1510"><span offset-key="d5a887c4672b42c885de063ec6aa1510:0">, we will introduce a new concept of "state". State allows React components to change their output over time in response to user actions, network responses, and anything else, without violating this rule.</span></span>

# 

<span key="5ca8b71fce27488c9b2f954ba4c47224">**State and Lifecycle**</span>

# 

<span key="8cde8a466cbc4384bb0afa346e4d7d7d"><span offset-key="8cde8a466cbc4384bb0afa346e4d7d7d:0">This page introduces the concept of state and lifecycle in a React component. You can find a </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/react-component.html" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="3a6c7696e2dc40fca88de55ef2b032ed" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="fbe2461b25304d8cacddaf051c8ea323"><span data-offset-key="fbe2461b25304d8cacddaf051c8ea323:0">detailed component API reference here</span></span></span></a><span key="d253f2ddda294f96a208656d556ddaad"><span offset-key="d253f2ddda294f96a208656d556ddaad:0">.</span></span>

<span key="18d79aef588247c2aa86e08a3f7f5e4c"><span offset-key="18d79aef588247c2aa86e08a3f7f5e4c:0">Consider the ticking clock example from </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/rendering-elements.html#updating-the-rendered-element" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="9bdbb03dd12f4a2b9def5848e559701d" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="dc8c0b7eb291425d9f146798c6b4d46d"><span data-offset-key="dc8c0b7eb291425d9f146798c6b4d46d:0">one of the previous sections</span></span></span></a><span key="445cc6e7e3d5483cabec7d6355ffd246"><span offset-key="445cc6e7e3d5483cabec7d6355ffd246:0">. In </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/rendering-elements.html#rendering-an-element-into-the-dom" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="041384209ffa489db82d99e9c2a9eb59" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="2ed89859ed2945ad85335c0e039b046e"><span data-offset-key="2ed89859ed2945ad85335c0e039b046e:0">Rendering Elements</span></span></span></a><span key="6741ce601bc14105996760fcb2a638e5"><span offset-key="6741ce601bc14105996760fcb2a638e5:0">, we have only learned one way to update the UI. We call ReactDOM.render() to change the rendered output:</span></span>

<span key="36187922788948c099b59b019d186136"><span offset-key="36187922788948c099b59b019d186136:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/gwoJZk?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="50b42e20f26e469db286f86783f1209b" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="da3572cc11ee4d58a34169d56e418cbf"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="380f9f0526894b638cbd0ae9579445de"><span offset-key="380f9f0526894b638cbd0ae9579445de:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="04093e9d9bf442c2b2891384f4466c1b"><span offset-key="04093e9d9bf442c2b2891384f4466c1b:0">In this section, we will learn how to make the Clock component truly reusable and encapsulated. It will set up its own timer and update itself every second.</span></span>

<span key="a7d1703d4062425bb7344b82b3f25b35"><span offset-key="a7d1703d4062425bb7344b82b3f25b35:0">We can start by encapsulating how the clock looks:</span></span>

<span key="ae87f7215a254931aaa9a67155ae447a"><span offset-key="ae87f7215a254931aaa9a67155ae447a:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/dpdoYR?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="bc9ca2e4dbf24391b75c35b922ae2256" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="e91beaf40ebf4c7cbc9afce6fd858020"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="00960fc5e24641da813b6f9782a36fae"><span offset-key="00960fc5e24641da813b6f9782a36fae:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="538c221e972442cdadea30fbccf06449"><span offset-key="538c221e972442cdadea30fbccf06449:0">However, it misses a crucial requirement: the fact that the Clock sets up a timer and updates the UI every second should be an implementation detail of the Clock.</span></span>

<span key="21c80a9e8a73477687a030deb8a63357"><span offset-key="21c80a9e8a73477687a030deb8a63357:0">Ideally we want to write this once and have the Clock update itself:</span></span>

<span key="772f018404f34dcbbda05a5836ddf9f3"><span offset-key="772f018404f34dcbbda05a5836ddf9f3:0">To implement this, we need to add "state" to the Clock component.</span></span>

<span key="3d62e833e6624048942528e27ec38c64"><span offset-key="3d62e833e6624048942528e27ec38c64:0">State is similar to props, but it is private and fully controlled by the component.</span></span>

# 

<span key="1bffb9fbcdec459497253e417021b088"><span offset-key="1bffb9fbcdec459497253e417021b088:0">Converting a Function to a Class</span></span>

<span key="1f0491348cbd4a50833e7bbf131f9376"><span offset-key="1f0491348cbd4a50833e7bbf131f9376:0">You can convert a function component like Clock to a class in five steps:</span></span>

1.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">1.</span>
    <span key="ebca7ede476a47e7975610f39af8daa9"><span offset-key="ebca7ede476a47e7975610f39af8daa9:0">Create an </span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Classes" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="125528b7e41b4d48b938ab514303a590" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="e0256c845b6e49269e3f11d8b8e4dc6e"><span data-offset-key="e0256c845b6e49269e3f11d8b8e4dc6e:0">ES6 class</span></span></span></a><span key="ccbb981ed29940578c883f395d3ad1ee"><span offset-key="ccbb981ed29940578c883f395d3ad1ee:0">, with the same name, that extends React.Component.</span></span>

2.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">2.</span>
    <span key="bdaaaa88ae904ea7b03a1345ae0cf491"><span offset-key="bdaaaa88ae904ea7b03a1345ae0cf491:0">Add a single empty method to it called render().</span></span>

3.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">3.</span>
    <span key="256a4b72719443c8a18ffef5396e81ad"><span offset-key="256a4b72719443c8a18ffef5396e81ad:0">Move the body of the function into the render() method.</span></span>

4.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">4.</span>
    <span key="2413458ca6d640e48beea1e41b0d3300"><span offset-key="2413458ca6d640e48beea1e41b0d3300:0">Replace props with this.props in the render() body.</span></span>

5.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">5.</span>
    <span key="3585ef5f109649b3b1d18be1e6ebd76e"><span offset-key="3585ef5f109649b3b1d18be1e6ebd76e:0">Delete the remaining empty function declaration.</span></span>

<span key="0d5488cb6548449e8e3acc5d78feaa74"><span offset-key="0d5488cb6548449e8e3acc5d78feaa74:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/zKRGpo?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="fff9454ddc74494ca4d6a1d4eeff837f" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="54cf724d30904667a8129823d157e35c"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="1f7fa943541841169356767371fdbf64"><span offset-key="1f7fa943541841169356767371fdbf64:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="d7c6bd01dcc6499a8fd33e7ef86f335d"><span offset-key="d7c6bd01dcc6499a8fd33e7ef86f335d:0">Clock is now defined as a class rather than a function.</span></span>

<span key="5d5a7dbf95c340c58a4431deed7b2ba9"><span offset-key="5d5a7dbf95c340c58a4431deed7b2ba9:0">The render method will be called each time an update happens, but as long as we render &lt;Clock /> into the same DOM node, only a single instance of the Clock class will be used. This lets us use additional features such as local state and lifecycle methods.</span></span>

# 

<span key="aace217b0832497bb377fb97c9923e88"><span offset-key="aace217b0832497bb377fb97c9923e88:0">Adding Local State to a Class</span></span>

<span key="2101098bca124062af7104e8d73813d5"><span offset-key="2101098bca124062af7104e8d73813d5:0">We will move the date from props to state in three steps:</span></span>

1.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">1.</span>
    <span key="cf1e79a8e4e24ae9a6218b9377e607c7"><span offset-key="cf1e79a8e4e24ae9a6218b9377e607c7:0">Replace this.props.date with this.state.date in the render() method:</span></span>

2.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">2.</span>
    <span key="f434c115961245e8be424e28597d1b87"><span offset-key="f434c115961245e8be424e28597d1b87:0">Add a </span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Classes#Constructor" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="18fe9b170412440bae62caa40949d338" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="d1d19255772b48a19523f40d3f265e0a"><span data-offset-key="d1d19255772b48a19523f40d3f265e0a:0">class constructor</span></span></span></a><span key="7bf001346c7c4bc2b48d6f325b46b24f"><span offset-key="7bf001346c7c4bc2b48d6f325b46b24f:0"> that assigns the initial this.state:</span></span>

<span key="78717d5d43d24dc4aa72654320e9cfb9"><span offset-key="78717d5d43d24dc4aa72654320e9cfb9:0">Note how we pass props to the base constructor:</span></span>

<span key="5b19607fe5cf4b5abfb53ea87bb3cb5a"><span offset-key="5b19607fe5cf4b5abfb53ea87bb3cb5a:0">Class components should always call the base constructor with props.</span></span>

1.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">1.</span>
    <span key="a8cedcfcb382408299113cb0bab1c84d"><span offset-key="a8cedcfcb382408299113cb0bab1c84d:0">Remove the date prop from the &lt;Clock /> element:</span></span>

<span key="c49502c71c5b4c418ee49604a8de17a5"><span offset-key="c49502c71c5b4c418ee49604a8de17a5:0">We will later add the timer code back to the component itself.</span></span>

<span key="b8ffc039db564979bbc24b14289c23ad"><span offset-key="b8ffc039db564979bbc24b14289c23ad:0">The result looks like this:</span></span>

<span key="c4e277766ce84cab8b0085e20a55a420"><span offset-key="c4e277766ce84cab8b0085e20a55a420:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/KgQpJd?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="b6f34ea9596a408d8c9c71c064178a47" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="f5aa6abd739c4057adbaeaec081a9b4f"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="95d9a395d48346ab9937a593989b6ea4"><span offset-key="95d9a395d48346ab9937a593989b6ea4:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="8426da060d2649babc9399c01c32e35a"><span offset-key="8426da060d2649babc9399c01c32e35a:0">Next, we'll make the Clock set up its own timer and update itself every second.</span></span>

# 

<span key="68c33c4b5328478f8070a8d5b01d0e44"><span offset-key="68c33c4b5328478f8070a8d5b01d0e44:0">Adding Lifecycle Methods to a Class</span></span>

<span key="4108a346e7b7437e90c71b4e7388ba4c"><span offset-key="4108a346e7b7437e90c71b4e7388ba4c:0">In applications with many components, it's very important to free up resources taken by the components when they are destroyed.</span></span>

<span key="280709fa56f540f5843a907eeda60abf"><span offset-key="280709fa56f540f5843a907eeda60abf:0">We want to </span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/WindowTimers/setInterval" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="c3cd944963ef44d692bb8d744d7272a4" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="a68743a283354e069432cb7a38254a1f"><span data-offset-key="a68743a283354e069432cb7a38254a1f:0">set up a timer</span></span></span></a><span key="80a72b230e7a4cd4ac52f3fdd1bc36db"><span offset-key="80a72b230e7a4cd4ac52f3fdd1bc36db:0"> whenever the Clock is rendered to the DOM for the first time. This is called "mounting" in React.</span></span>

<span key="d4be48de64884ba68bf18d9596d4d9ed"><span offset-key="d4be48de64884ba68bf18d9596d4d9ed:0">We also want to </span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/WindowTimers/clearInterval" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="051a1ac4f3b44d4f94858f497bf7b886" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="b9b51a8a9a264737bc2cfb28757f2c82"><span data-offset-key="b9b51a8a9a264737bc2cfb28757f2c82:0">clear that timer</span></span></span></a><span key="1568c2019d7f4dd18cf31e2a59ae2d4f"><span offset-key="1568c2019d7f4dd18cf31e2a59ae2d4f:0"> whenever the DOM produced by the Clock is removed. This is called "unmounting" in React.</span></span>

<span key="f14a219c7f33414faa988e17ec88c602"><span offset-key="f14a219c7f33414faa988e17ec88c602:0">We can declare special methods on the component class to run some code when a component mounts and unmounts:</span></span>

<span key="1a199863796e49ff88915cbd0b9ed33f"><span offset-key="1a199863796e49ff88915cbd0b9ed33f:0">These methods are called "lifecycle methods".</span></span>

<span key="d3d96e1119fa4b1bab9d74e8498ff666"><span offset-key="d3d96e1119fa4b1bab9d74e8498ff666:0">The componentDidMount() method runs after the component output has been rendered to the DOM. This is a good place to set up a timer:</span></span>

<span key="2687e4e6ab8240ae8df456fcd2b4b8ad"><span offset-key="2687e4e6ab8240ae8df456fcd2b4b8ad:0">Note how we save the timer ID right on this (this.timerID).</span></span>

<span key="0984b1cf9dca454ba93d980717a28262"><span offset-key="0984b1cf9dca454ba93d980717a28262:0">While this.props is set up by React itself and this.state has a special meaning, you are free to add additional fields to the class manually if you need to store something that doesn't participate in the data flow (like a timer ID).</span></span>

<span key="c571168bac85437996414e6c2b21a022"><span offset-key="c571168bac85437996414e6c2b21a022:0">We will tear down the timer in the componentWillUnmount() lifecycle method:</span></span>

<span key="eab337a99aa94521aa0380da29fac97a"><span offset-key="eab337a99aa94521aa0380da29fac97a:0">Finally, we will implement a method called tick() that the Clock component will run every second.</span></span>

<span key="610a2f5935954c0d81d92b284b4e2798"><span offset-key="610a2f5935954c0d81d92b284b4e2798:0">It will use this.setState() to schedule updates to the component local state:</span></span>

<span key="8d440997c8594701a66f9098c45a6cc8"><span offset-key="8d440997c8594701a66f9098c45a6cc8:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/amqdNA?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="79161ca4b2574508939edbd0d7d8031c" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="92e1e816af3f41bfabc7a5655db19e63"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="3e627323174345158ab5c86c846bd0b4"><span offset-key="3e627323174345158ab5c86c846bd0b4:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="d6a721fdee5f456da119b27603762c12"><span offset-key="d6a721fdee5f456da119b27603762c12:0">Now the clock ticks every second.</span></span>

<span key="b967a1dbe2214229877630add865270a"><span offset-key="b967a1dbe2214229877630add865270a:0">Let's quickly recap what's going on and the order in which the methods are called:</span></span>

1.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">1.</span>
    <span key="ff00d3a009174b9cabe0990f7fda8973"><span offset-key="ff00d3a009174b9cabe0990f7fda8973:0">When &lt;Clock /> is passed to ReactDOM.render(), React calls the constructor of the Clock component. Since Clock needs to display the current time, it initializes this.state with an object including the current time. We will later update this state.</span></span>

2.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">2.</span>
    <span key="14fb1a7f278a4964889b4020fa049d4e"><span offset-key="14fb1a7f278a4964889b4020fa049d4e:0">React then calls the Clock component's render() method. This is how React learns what should be displayed on the screen. React then updates the DOM to match the Clock's render output.</span></span>

3.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">3.</span>
    <span key="991a5a0e8fed4997baac01530883944a"><span offset-key="991a5a0e8fed4997baac01530883944a:0">When the Clock output is inserted in the DOM, React calls the componentDidMount() lifecycle method. Inside it, the Clock component asks the browser to set up a timer to call the component's tick() method once a second.</span></span>

4.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">4.</span>
    <span key="5ae8707ae5bb41a99af95a3e5770dd11"><span offset-key="5ae8707ae5bb41a99af95a3e5770dd11:0">Every second the browser calls the tick() method. Inside it, the Clock component schedules a UI update by calling setState() with an object containing the current time. Thanks to the setState() call, React knows the state has changed, and calls the render() method again to learn what should be on the screen. This time, this.state.date in the render() method will be different, and so the render output will include the updated time. React updates the DOM accordingly.</span></span>

5.  <span class="r-1awozwy r-1nf4jbm r-6koalj r-18u37iz r-gg6oyi r-ubezar r-16dba41 r-135wba7 r-1m04atk r-1pyaxff" contenteditable="false" style="height:24px">5.</span>
    <span key="dc3e22211ead41f9b29b2cf1ad7b1668"><span offset-key="dc3e22211ead41f9b29b2cf1ad7b1668:0">If the Clock component is ever removed from the DOM, React calls the componentWillUnmount() lifecycle method so the timer is stopped.</span></span>

# 

<span key="ac3f20f92518414499d1983d76c7e2cb"><span offset-key="ac3f20f92518414499d1983d76c7e2cb:0">Using State Correctly</span></span>

<span key="7067f99295d5403b99974c2ec8d42af0"><span offset-key="7067f99295d5403b99974c2ec8d42af0:0">There are three things you should know about setState().</span></span>

# 

<span key="467bb71ebca142e8a8f1277c1c653264"><span offset-key="467bb71ebca142e8a8f1277c1c653264:0">Do Not Modify State Directly</span></span>

<span key="e9e15bb2b4de49b1bf83f1be01d94757"><span offset-key="e9e15bb2b4de49b1bf83f1be01d94757:0">For example, this will not re-render a component:</span></span>

<span key="7ddc9c8916ae4af08683661363723044"><span offset-key="7ddc9c8916ae4af08683661363723044:0">Instead, use setState():</span></span>

<span key="a92e179cc33c41fab407efd2761599d1"><span offset-key="a92e179cc33c41fab407efd2761599d1:0">The only place where you can assign this.state is the constructor.</span></span>

# 

<span key="03654e5bb6ea4d9590cf6d3d158f0795"><span offset-key="03654e5bb6ea4d9590cf6d3d158f0795:0">State Updates May Be Asynchronous</span></span>

<span key="73da05cc782f4f80b0f0b4a8a864c9e9"><span offset-key="73da05cc782f4f80b0f0b4a8a864c9e9:0">React may batch multiple setState() calls into a single update for performance.</span></span>

<span key="0553353b490440398b19e974729270b2"><span offset-key="0553353b490440398b19e974729270b2:0">Because this.props and this.state may be updated asynchronously, you should not rely on their values for calculating the next state.</span></span>

<span key="2d4f943d7f934176b9ac1ab872714215"><span offset-key="2d4f943d7f934176b9ac1ab872714215:0">For example, this code may fail to update the counter:</span></span>

<span key="54eed935b730407483000db0aba35edd"><span offset-key="54eed935b730407483000db0aba35edd:0">To fix it, use a second form of setState() that accepts a function rather than an object. That function will receive the previous state as the first argument, and the props at the time the update is applied as the second argument:</span></span>

<span key="46bd330f851c4a1aa5edbb6746931a12"><span offset-key="46bd330f851c4a1aa5edbb6746931a12:0">We used an </span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Functions/Arrow_functions" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="80679c383b064e858be134c9ed2c23fd" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="dd93c848835348a6b89db6742d6be7f9"><span data-offset-key="dd93c848835348a6b89db6742d6be7f9:0">arrow function</span></span></span></a><span key="39e24aa5e3eb4c0c8500c0c0d209eeef"><span offset-key="39e24aa5e3eb4c0c8500c0c0d209eeef:0"> above, but it also works with regular functions:</span></span>

# 

<span key="ab6f3640a3b14daeb2982e6163787e62"><span offset-key="ab6f3640a3b14daeb2982e6163787e62:0">State Updates are Merged</span></span>

<span key="0292a007b95f442084f651e5e2431176"><span offset-key="0292a007b95f442084f651e5e2431176:0">When you call setState(), React merges the object you provide into the current state.</span></span>

<span key="2b49d35e887d462a8581b1459ede3402"><span offset-key="2b49d35e887d462a8581b1459ede3402:0">For example, your state may contain several independent variables:</span></span>

<span key="256b2d0f3d2741e0ace1426069327016"><span offset-key="256b2d0f3d2741e0ace1426069327016:0">Then you can update them independently with separate setState() calls:</span></span>

<span key="72b6aa22f214491da943d4073f2bfc33"><span offset-key="72b6aa22f214491da943d4073f2bfc33:0">The merging is shallow, so this.setState({comments}) leaves this.state.posts intact, but completely replaces this.state.comments.</span></span>

# 

<span key="b948d30ca698420a9295f9e5120ea62a"><span offset-key="b948d30ca698420a9295f9e5120ea62a:0">The Data Flows Down</span></span>

<span key="e641856693ff48a7ac10ab50dbbaee05"><span offset-key="e641856693ff48a7ac10ab50dbbaee05:0">Neither parent nor child components can know if a certain component is stateful or stateless, and they shouldn't care whether it is defined as a function or a class.</span></span>

<span key="3e0ef1c5eaf044a5a3fb20ae78d55654"><span offset-key="3e0ef1c5eaf044a5a3fb20ae78d55654:0">This is why state is often called local or encapsulated. It is not accessible to any component other than the one that owns and sets it.</span></span>

<span key="76d5fd78ca8d4004b8e62e04eaed490b"><span offset-key="76d5fd78ca8d4004b8e62e04eaed490b:0">A component may choose to pass its state down as props to its child components:</span></span>

<span key="0f670fc4a2814b60b624cfdf0ed88a57"><span offset-key="0f670fc4a2814b60b624cfdf0ed88a57:0">The FormattedDate component would receive the date in its props and wouldn't know whether it came from the Clock's state, from the Clock's props, or was typed by hand:</span></span>

<span key="8df545d7ab6049d3aa680dc56cb4cb70"><span offset-key="8df545d7ab6049d3aa680dc56cb4cb70:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/zKRqNB?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="8b647887547e48dfbd5ec594eb0fda39" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="271b857bb51b4b36ab4eaddcb0e7dc9e"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="94912336ff4347c489900ecc4ae4f944"><span offset-key="94912336ff4347c489900ecc4ae4f944:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="a7f9d3b6c2854edbaba2bf1abd038af2"><span offset-key="a7f9d3b6c2854edbaba2bf1abd038af2:0">This is commonly called a "top-down" or "unidirectional" data flow. Any state is always owned by some specific component, and any data or UI derived from that state can only affect components "below" them in the tree.</span></span>

<span key="a304a34c684d473089237ac0bcb4f2dc"><span offset-key="a304a34c684d473089237ac0bcb4f2dc:0">If you imagine a component tree as a waterfall of props, each component's state is like an additional water source that joins it at an arbitrary point but also flows down.</span></span>

<span key="32d9d1e3e84542e58a8949ba27f90024"><span offset-key="32d9d1e3e84542e58a8949ba27f90024:0">To show that all components are truly isolated, we can create an App component that renders three &lt;Clock>s:</span></span>

<span key="f96dd928fe9a4eeb81804651aae8993d"><span offset-key="f96dd928fe9a4eeb81804651aae8993d:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/vXdGmd?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="de34104616ce476ab318e4c85119f27e" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="1055b1562c514b96b4a2928b6cf7a36a"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="1e02ef023ca34904bb4d513e5e487be1"><span offset-key="1e02ef023ca34904bb4d513e5e487be1:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="9defba2859b4467690101774b053fb0a"><span offset-key="9defba2859b4467690101774b053fb0a:0">Each Clock sets up its own timer and updates independently.</span></span>

<span key="8702a318b52f4eba8a7cdd8beeb92153"><span offset-key="8702a318b52f4eba8a7cdd8beeb92153:0">In React apps, whether a component is stateful or stateless is considered an implementation detail of the component that may change over time. You can use stateless components inside stateful components, and vice versa.</span></span>

# 

<span key="721ff7c84836469aa6a7e6a9249aa8f4">**Handling Events**</span>

#
