<span key="788286f74b5d4edbb6423fd9d227f215"><span offset-key="788286f74b5d4edbb6423fd9d227f215:0">Handling events with React elements is very similar to handling events on DOM elements. There are some syntax differences:</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSIgc3R5bGU9ImhlaWdodDoxMnB4O3ZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm" />

    <span key="fb10997b019e4098b903658f56c9ba38"><span offset-key="fb10997b019e4098b903658f56c9ba38:0">React events are named using camelCase, rather than lowercase.</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSIgc3R5bGU9ImhlaWdodDoxMnB4O3ZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm" />

    <span key="761dec9c801f497c99b14ada63019208"><span offset-key="761dec9c801f497c99b14ada63019208:0">With JSX you pass a function as the event handler, rather than a string.</span></span>

<span key="98d2aacef57040eba8c81e8d90364148"><span offset-key="98d2aacef57040eba8c81e8d90364148:0">For example, the HTML:</span></span>

<span key="de35d686221a455496a698e12bc0bfad"><span offset-key="de35d686221a455496a698e12bc0bfad:0">is slightly different in React:</span></span>

<span key="ab3e3fb541714b14a723b93b50ba1cec"><span offset-key="ab3e3fb541714b14a723b93b50ba1cec:0">Another difference is that you cannot return false to prevent default behavior in React. You must call preventDefault explicitly. For example, with plain HTML, to prevent the default form behavior of submitting, you can write:</span></span>

<span key="adbfba9f83ac4681803ce579acd61e0b"><span offset-key="adbfba9f83ac4681803ce579acd61e0b:0">In React, this could instead be:</span></span>

<span key="4f63004b4b434512981cfb5a4b436a20"><span offset-key="4f63004b4b434512981cfb5a4b436a20:0">Here, e is a synthetic event. React defines these synthetic events according to the </span></span><a href="https://www.w3.org/TR/DOM-Level-3-Events/" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="62b19040af2e419ab67454d40a273202" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="29d0c91132884d5fa6b3784ceeb11408"><span data-offset-key="29d0c91132884d5fa6b3784ceeb11408:0">W3C spec</span></span></span></a><span key="d002dabeed264b53b64803c33e37d570"><span offset-key="d002dabeed264b53b64803c33e37d570:0">, so you don't need to worry about cross-browser compatibility. React events do not work exactly the same as native events. See the \[SyntheticEvent\](&lt;</span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/events.html%3E" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="1c6ad50029c146c29b37ef5f8dfa2e8c" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="1db2eef94bad43e1b4a83779559a0f0d"><span data-offset-key="1db2eef94bad43e1b4a83779559a0f0d:0">https://reactjs.org/docs/events.html&gt;</span></span></span></a><span key="621b0f3a41704eb0a9d61dc17b3466bf"><span offset-key="621b0f3a41704eb0a9d61dc17b3466bf:0">) reference guide to learn more.</span></span>

<span key="91664858bf474c27ba924a4dfd80702c"><span offset-key="91664858bf474c27ba924a4dfd80702c:0">When using React, you generally don't need to call addEventListener to add listeners to a DOM element after it is created. Instead, just provide a listener when the element is initially rendered.</span></span>

<span key="22b8d82bbc754f5794cab19bc7bec75e"><span offset-key="22b8d82bbc754f5794cab19bc7bec75e:0">When you define a component using an </span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Classes" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="d1370b8aef644dfbbfebaddc004e7820" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="077a885175904071a433e714d1b1b2d1"><span data-offset-key="077a885175904071a433e714d1b1b2d1:0">ES6 class</span></span></span></a><span key="77d97596b9d349a89e2f4fb08d4db529"><span offset-key="77d97596b9d349a89e2f4fb08d4db529:0">, a common pattern is for an event handler to be a method on the class. For example, this Toggle component renders a button that lets the user toggle between "ON" and "OFF" states:</span></span>

<span key="3d4836b4e5864c05bc9467bd6ce544d3"><span offset-key="3d4836b4e5864c05bc9467bd6ce544d3:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/xEmzGg?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="88bec51aa2614fb1a9fd894a7cf150d5" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="1557396aaafc4e9a8ea5870b7f74f4bd"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="9719a9ed97de49349247d62d157735ac"><span offset-key="9719a9ed97de49349247d62d157735ac:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="e1b4c19198184378b7db31c2420c8e9b"><span offset-key="e1b4c19198184378b7db31c2420c8e9b:0">You have to be careful about the meaning of this in JSX callbacks. In JavaScript, class methods are not </span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_objects/Function/bind" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="6541ba7e43f64347b5b3b17e0890d37e" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="550d1a107cfc438daa608ecbc4881804"><span data-offset-key="550d1a107cfc438daa608ecbc4881804:0">bound</span></span></span></a><span key="25bada66a0934a17a76e7be388d3db01"><span offset-key="25bada66a0934a17a76e7be388d3db01:0"> by default. If you forget to bind this.handleClick and pass it to onClick, this will be undefined when the function is actually called.</span></span>

<span key="63ee6bdeb5114d5e9225c0c02896bbb7"><span offset-key="63ee6bdeb5114d5e9225c0c02896bbb7:0">This is not React-specific behavior; it is a part of </span></span><a href="https://www.smashingmagazine.com/2014/01/understanding-javascript-function-prototype-bind/" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="9b07691e7eef4e6a9485c5deffe25e16" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="aea24ad5d2bc4c0784d6fc182f3dd1a6"><span data-offset-key="aea24ad5d2bc4c0784d6fc182f3dd1a6:0">how functions work in JavaScript</span></span></span></a><span key="66094aac974d4b89a875256d4ecef258"><span offset-key="66094aac974d4b89a875256d4ecef258:0">. Generally, if you refer to a method without () after it, such as onClick={this.handleClick}, you should bind that method.</span></span>

<span key="7946309dbc134bda8b87c2b28e8de889"><span offset-key="7946309dbc134bda8b87c2b28e8de889:0">If calling bind annoys you, there are two ways you can get around this. If you are using the experimental </span></span><a href="https://babeljs.io/docs/plugins/transform-class-properties/" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="2916aca09d5747708d0e13b8e26f265d" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="e444cc7817034795a0a48748cf410b96"><span data-offset-key="e444cc7817034795a0a48748cf410b96:0">public class fields syntax</span></span></span></a><span key="a08d7b1f33974aa89bf192afc6f3fd1a"><span offset-key="a08d7b1f33974aa89bf192afc6f3fd1a:0">, you can use class fields to correctly bind callbacks:</span></span>

<span key="8a307a439d2e4440a903b8573e79aee5"><span offset-key="8a307a439d2e4440a903b8573e79aee5:0">This syntax is enabled by default in </span></span><a href="https://github.com/facebookincubator/create-react-app" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="24e90c8e379b46d0b0d5bee0725804bd" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="8137513b34344a399a582eeb44c3ada0"><span data-offset-key="8137513b34344a399a582eeb44c3ada0:0">Create React App</span></span></span></a><span key="9d12919aa5104bccab11ea4875086c3e"><span offset-key="9d12919aa5104bccab11ea4875086c3e:0">.</span></span>

<span key="36458767f9b7473a88df987eb484ab78"><span offset-key="36458767f9b7473a88df987eb484ab78:0">If you aren't using class fields syntax, you can use an </span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Functions/Arrow_functions" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="5946c2a567e74cb786e60d39d395c93d" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="7b92e18df82946808359911b41a15a99"><span data-offset-key="7b92e18df82946808359911b41a15a99:0">arrow function</span></span></span></a><span key="814adb82148241e1af7d69509ae398a7"><span offset-key="814adb82148241e1af7d69509ae398a7:0"> in the callback:</span></span>

<span key="9fbd3e10605c41b49f2aa8b04d8f4f32"><span offset-key="9fbd3e10605c41b49f2aa8b04d8f4f32:0">The problem with this syntax is that a different callback is created each time the LoggingButton renders. In most cases, this is fine. However, if this callback is passed as a prop to lower components, those components might do an extra re-rendering. We generally recommend binding in the constructor or using the class fields syntax, to avoid this sort of performance problem.</span></span>

# 

<span key="77003def665f426cba6288f6dc69bfe2"><span offset-key="77003def665f426cba6288f6dc69bfe2:0">Passing Arguments to Event Handlers</span></span>

<span key="88d39efe2ad5426ebf70b7f1025e1a0e"><span offset-key="88d39efe2ad5426ebf70b7f1025e1a0e:0">Inside a loop, it is common to want to pass an extra parameter to an event handler. For example, if id is the row ID, either of the following would work:</span></span>

<span key="aa395af048a042db998afd12e785fcb0"><span offset-key="aa395af048a042db998afd12e785fcb0:0">&lt;button onClick={(e) => this.deleteRow(id, e)}>Delete Row&lt;/button>&lt;button onClick={this.deleteRow.bind(this, id)}>Delete Row&lt;/button></span></span>

<span key="0222c11b913342d2b840ea9d22bdd994"><span offset-key="0222c11b913342d2b840ea9d22bdd994:0">The above two lines are equivalent, and use </span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Functions/Arrow_functions" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="7516834e68074fa6befde793ea51ec1a" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="36882ab8d0864f458a5d4cc6782c3d22"><span data-offset-key="36882ab8d0864f458a5d4cc6782c3d22:0">arrow functions</span></span></span></a><span key="f5339bcea0af42eb8cc02069ee74e611"><span offset-key="f5339bcea0af42eb8cc02069ee74e611:0"> and \[Function.prototype.bind\](&lt;</span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_objects/Function/bind%3E" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="11c832f339ff48028c2f4c9f5099f23e" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="cefd4f59fb5649c8a2a882785c74a544"><span data-offset-key="cefd4f59fb5649c8a2a882785c74a544:0">https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_objects/Function/bind&gt;</span></span></span></a><span key="d31599b19e5a4fa39d3e8def4b026e07"><span offset-key="d31599b19e5a4fa39d3e8def4b026e07:0">) respectively.</span></span>

<span key="2fcdcfb0469148e3b5a3e2d33b8b1033"><span offset-key="2fcdcfb0469148e3b5a3e2d33b8b1033:0">In both cases, the e argument representing the React event will be passed as a second argument after the ID. With an arrow function, we have to pass it explicitly, but with bind any further arguments are automatically forwarded.</span></span>

# 

<span key="c375370e1a02448092bc5776e1a75f5e">**Conditional Rendering**</span>

# 

<span key="76123e58e3734a3a9f1ca45926b79208"><span offset-key="76123e58e3734a3a9f1ca45926b79208:0">In React, you can create distinct components that encapsulate behavior you need. Then, you can render only some of them, depending on the state of your application.</span></span>

<span key="18378da5b8314c1a93dc95de451c6722"><span offset-key="18378da5b8314c1a93dc95de451c6722:0">Conditional rendering in React works the same way conditions work in JavaScript. Use JavaScript operators like \[if\](&lt;</span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Statements/if...else%3E" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="0aae28330f6f4b88b83699fdde6fe371" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="8c4d7a98ebfc40588902917596f2d585"><span data-offset-key="8c4d7a98ebfc40588902917596f2d585:0">https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Statements/if...else&gt;</span></span></span></a><span key="6be674f283c34491b3d65fd40a1cc5f1"><span offset-key="6be674f283c34491b3d65fd40a1cc5f1:0">) or the </span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Operators/Conditional_Operator" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="6153a1ec46684cd685505f358fcf245f" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="492ca1cd0a5e4787b5560bd98665768c"><span data-offset-key="492ca1cd0a5e4787b5560bd98665768c:0">conditional operator</span></span></span></a><span key="c7c0dfa2b03f4a5190772e7083240215"><span offset-key="c7c0dfa2b03f4a5190772e7083240215:0"> to create elements representing the current state, and let React update the UI to match them.</span></span>

<span key="f44972104cb548d59fe4c3e2172a84d9"><span offset-key="f44972104cb548d59fe4c3e2172a84d9:0">Consider these two components:</span></span>

<span key="5dbd09aafc024dec83cdc9b1d890e9e2"><span offset-key="5dbd09aafc024dec83cdc9b1d890e9e2:0">We'll create a Greeting component that displays either of these components depending on whether a user is logged in:</span></span>

<span key="5f93920070a04b00adcf9a1be4fc44c1"><span offset-key="5f93920070a04b00adcf9a1be4fc44c1:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/ZpVxNq?editors=0011" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="0409c10f09fd47908ccc65140221ea52" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="5ce8aa3ca8ed4436942be3b727fc1ed4"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="4cf4a63d8b654b278e3eaea7887ebe8c"><span offset-key="4cf4a63d8b654b278e3eaea7887ebe8c:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="e40c8e7b987a4cf4a1e23e8a911c3a09"><span offset-key="e40c8e7b987a4cf4a1e23e8a911c3a09:0">This example renders a different greeting depending on the value of isLoggedIn prop.</span></span>

# 

<span key="0d0be8a1abc247f7bfef94f3ab0ab8b0"><span offset-key="0d0be8a1abc247f7bfef94f3ab0ab8b0:0">Element Variables</span></span>

<span key="6460fa0797c847e98710bd2591f18b5b"><span offset-key="6460fa0797c847e98710bd2591f18b5b:0">You can use variables to store elements. This can help you conditionally render a part of the component while the rest of the output doesn't change.</span></span>

<span key="102806274f4b42dcab6af791f558b6b4"><span offset-key="102806274f4b42dcab6af791f558b6b4:0">Consider these two new components representing Logout and Login buttons:</span></span>

<span key="ac664b10946f47039e24632d84bb5174"><span offset-key="ac664b10946f47039e24632d84bb5174:0">In the example below, we will create a </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/state-and-lifecycle.html#adding-local-state-to-a-class" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="a9817f349f9c4fe595fe8219949267a6" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="b58dd3c8df6347ad980c026e545f8620"><span data-offset-key="b58dd3c8df6347ad980c026e545f8620:0">stateful component</span></span></span></a><span key="5a4e63ccb78c49bcb13c1c1a24394ae0"><span offset-key="5a4e63ccb78c49bcb13c1c1a24394ae0:0"> called LoginControl.</span></span>

<span key="c2a56fd908ed465fa63d7407d05c02bc"><span offset-key="c2a56fd908ed465fa63d7407d05c02bc:0">It will render either &lt;LoginButton /> or &lt;LogoutButton /> depending on its current state. It will also render a &lt;Greeting /> from the previous example:</span></span>

<span key="da5e1c4c37ac4592a5ff719e467fa2a2"><span offset-key="da5e1c4c37ac4592a5ff719e467fa2a2:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/QKzAgB?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="805c66c491554efbaa86ad7e86825861" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="b02259b2af504b04841bf8531f8965e0"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="c9d9d1e8b0fb4083b164be34a67633b9"><span offset-key="c9d9d1e8b0fb4083b164be34a67633b9:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="5479c0897d034c19a17d63055158ceb2"><span offset-key="5479c0897d034c19a17d63055158ceb2:0">While declaring a variable and using an if statement is a fine way to conditionally render a component, sometimes you might want to use a shorter syntax. There are a few ways to inline conditions in JSX, explained below.</span></span>

# 

<span key="a458c070bc794d7f819b5bf0c6bb4686"><span offset-key="a458c070bc794d7f819b5bf0c6bb4686:0">Inline If with Logical && Operator</span></span>

<span key="3285d69fa2b74240882ff5e346a85e08"><span offset-key="3285d69fa2b74240882ff5e346a85e08:0">You may </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/introducing-jsx.html#embedding-expressions-in-jsx" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="a2b09560b5a04e94831c3343f03c31c4" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="85f5f621f3d44de5a4a69c3b4c195c78"><span data-offset-key="85f5f621f3d44de5a4a69c3b4c195c78:0">embed expressions in JSX</span></span></span></a><span key="8a7198ff24984c1eb4afafda81e6541e"><span offset-key="8a7198ff24984c1eb4afafda81e6541e:0"> by wrapping them in curly braces. This includes the JavaScript logical && operator. It can be handy for conditionally including an element:</span></span>

<span key="f691a309cb7e462aaa37f48bd4e395b1"><span offset-key="f691a309cb7e462aaa37f48bd4e395b1:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/ozJddz?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="3818d6045c0545afae38393b14a308ff" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="540b46724f214308aa86081104c07fbb"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="57d1daf1e0064b71927ecabf5e78e03c"><span offset-key="57d1daf1e0064b71927ecabf5e78e03c:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="d0b55b9a4e6e4934a842cfc1f40bacfc"><span offset-key="d0b55b9a4e6e4934a842cfc1f40bacfc:0">It works because in JavaScript, true && expression always evaluates to expression, and false && expression always evaluates to false.</span></span>

<span key="4949e319819a49bfa2bfcfd5e8f9c842"><span offset-key="4949e319819a49bfa2bfcfd5e8f9c842:0">Therefore, if the condition is true, the element right after && will appear in the output. If it is false, React will ignore and skip it.</span></span>

<span key="ebe57db91bf74d6482f45ea5de2f4880"><span offset-key="ebe57db91bf74d6482f45ea5de2f4880:0">Note that returning a falsy expression will still cause the element after && to be skipped but will return the falsy expression. In the example below, &lt;div>0&lt;/div> will be returned by the render method.</span></span>

# 

<span key="93162c46608d4ff8ab079b1d60b9d7b8"><span offset-key="93162c46608d4ff8ab079b1d60b9d7b8:0">Inline If-Else with Conditional Operator</span></span>

<span key="cb6a213660a949b1a9157628092f4dde"><span offset-key="cb6a213660a949b1a9157628092f4dde:0">Another method for conditionally rendering elements inline is to use the JavaScript conditional operator \[condition ? true : false\](&lt;</span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Operators/Conditional_Operator%3E" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="2e3854f9915243beb027b8fde4932b30" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="188e7ee6ab6847d7afc53a72824bec70"><span data-offset-key="188e7ee6ab6847d7afc53a72824bec70:0">https://developer.mozilla.org/en/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Operators/Conditional_Operator&gt;</span></span></span></a><span key="4723c67bf0e445428513b651e7ae48a6"><span offset-key="4723c67bf0e445428513b651e7ae48a6:0">).</span></span>

<span key="e4370d7d38594f38bd68b76960937919"><span offset-key="e4370d7d38594f38bd68b76960937919:0">In the example below, we use it to conditionally render a small block of text.</span></span>

<span key="de1cc58fb2ef47d29379eecbe3e9b624"><span offset-key="de1cc58fb2ef47d29379eecbe3e9b624:0">It can also be used for larger expressions although it is less obvious what's going on:</span></span>

<span key="574c28fe1abb4286937e3bc3901034b1"><span offset-key="574c28fe1abb4286937e3bc3901034b1:0">Just like in JavaScript, it is up to you to choose an appropriate style based on what you and your team consider more readable. Also remember that whenever conditions become too complex, it might be a good time to </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/components-and-props.html#extracting-components" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="600cbf979133478dacefbb2c85004645" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="8c9c8c6bcb9f4fd3ba52f2ae60c28a88"><span data-offset-key="8c9c8c6bcb9f4fd3ba52f2ae60c28a88:0">extract a component</span></span></span></a><span key="811139f60884499b9593b139b60a3185"><span offset-key="811139f60884499b9593b139b60a3185:0">.</span></span>

# 

<span key="cb2d05c156474bcab4d599927df84832"><span offset-key="cb2d05c156474bcab4d599927df84832:0">Preventing Component from Rendering</span></span>

<span key="73725c17dc6e4667a7e0a65a47c02340"><span offset-key="73725c17dc6e4667a7e0a65a47c02340:0">In rare cases you might want a component to hide itself even though it was rendered by another component. To do this return null instead of its render output.</span></span>

<span key="8b15b4fe0a1c4f07bc87824f34ef06dd"><span offset-key="8b15b4fe0a1c4f07bc87824f34ef06dd:0">In the example below, the &lt;WarningBanner /> is rendered depending on the value of the prop called warn. If the value of the prop is false, then the component does not render:</span></span>

<span key="fb6211fefd4c4fcbabf38b771168df82"><span offset-key="fb6211fefd4c4fcbabf38b771168df82:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/Xjoqwm?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="10d4d2a30fa54ca0992fab4dc16c81c9" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="489987b03d9a4285963c313314a548c4"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="e5ac5c7cb9344a2ebfbde48d36845d19"><span offset-key="e5ac5c7cb9344a2ebfbde48d36845d19:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="40bc13e8474a427dbbafdf44fd521875"><span offset-key="40bc13e8474a427dbbafdf44fd521875:0">Returning null from a component's render method does not affect the firing of the component's lifecycle methods. For instance componentDidUpdate will still be called.</span></span>

# 

<span key="f46c1c20d03349e9b2bfc96dc44b3c65">**Lists and Keys**</span>

# 

<span key="519ed3f208a24bde94a382e24e22bd30"><span offset-key="519ed3f208a24bde94a382e24e22bd30:0">First, let's review how you transform lists in JavaScript.</span></span>

<span key="bfefa62dd4954efa98c3f4320c135b06"><span offset-key="bfefa62dd4954efa98c3f4320c135b06:0">Given the code below, we use the \[map()\](&lt;</span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Array/map%3E" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="23980898ee3a47f384bf3b39b6de12f9" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="10da0fa3245e409186bebc340abfeefc"><span data-offset-key="10da0fa3245e409186bebc340abfeefc:0">https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Array/map&gt;</span></span></span></a><span key="2c1fa4afb5c04c3aa6c325020a4cf48c"><span offset-key="2c1fa4afb5c04c3aa6c325020a4cf48c:0">) function to take an array of numbers and double their values. We assign the new array returned by map() to the variable doubled and log it:</span></span>

<span key="5e7173ce42e848cb824ee634f325a4b4"><span offset-key="5e7173ce42e848cb824ee634f325a4b4:0">This code logs \[2, 4, 6, 8, 10\] to the console.</span></span>

<span key="206b0dbf89d54c05aaa718b5b181dfe9"><span offset-key="206b0dbf89d54c05aaa718b5b181dfe9:0">In React, transforming arrays into lists of </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/rendering-elements.html" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="a6c891a6efa94e29b0b0b1ea88b032b7" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="e45895c553834dc89d4bddc2c6ff6477"><span data-offset-key="e45895c553834dc89d4bddc2c6ff6477:0">elements</span></span></span></a><span key="53ee9644b4be4ef8b9984bf16ba24eb7"><span offset-key="53ee9644b4be4ef8b9984bf16ba24eb7:0"> is nearly identical.</span></span>

# 

<span key="307fb750392e4d51a49687f16fd1be04"><span offset-key="307fb750392e4d51a49687f16fd1be04:0">Rendering Multiple Components</span></span>

<span key="6c322f2dce2f4c829c32a2f4db66f9dd"><span offset-key="6c322f2dce2f4c829c32a2f4db66f9dd:0">You can build collections of elements and </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/introducing-jsx.html#embedding-expressions-in-jsx" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="2ff84472a2f6444c84c4a1f8126f7614" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="628359e46d544d9889af0f1566e13476"><span data-offset-key="628359e46d544d9889af0f1566e13476:0">include them in JSX</span></span></span></a><span key="4513d0a2fbe54ee59e970b3869ccb3ed"><span offset-key="4513d0a2fbe54ee59e970b3869ccb3ed:0"> using curly braces {}.</span></span>

<span key="6883cfd2935042dca5f368584802f495"><span offset-key="6883cfd2935042dca5f368584802f495:0">Below, we loop through the numbers array using the JavaScript \[map()\](&lt;</span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Array/map%3E" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="2d2ebe3d325c45b9ae60c989953b7ac9" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="d07053f55af04b97af17b8503946cd7c"><span data-offset-key="d07053f55af04b97af17b8503946cd7c:0">https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Array/map&gt;</span></span></span></a><span key="f50dd53f38aa446bb7d94bc01320d7ff"><span offset-key="f50dd53f38aa446bb7d94bc01320d7ff:0">) function. We return a &lt;li> element for each item. Finally, we assign the resulting array of elements to listItems:</span></span>

<span key="2b40d280ae4f42d6869855e6d7a90366"><span offset-key="2b40d280ae4f42d6869855e6d7a90366:0">We include the entire listItems array inside a &lt;ul> element, and </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/rendering-elements.html#rendering-an-element-into-the-dom" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="fb5386e75e664e868f83b9f2f85f950b" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="3d24df1424be4b24834f9519c0644d40"><span data-offset-key="3d24df1424be4b24834f9519c0644d40:0">render it to the DOM</span></span></span></a><span key="c6042b3fd1224e03a377396297edc79c"><span offset-key="c6042b3fd1224e03a377396297edc79c:0">:</span></span>

<span key="450650613f1c42709242ef026de8f1bd"><span offset-key="450650613f1c42709242ef026de8f1bd:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/GjPyQr?editors=0011" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="90f23ea47cd343b987630d29fbe78f22" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="3ef2c4787e9348b4a89a1b075f700e24"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="2fc2e5cf74184e579caea1282b3be74f"><span offset-key="2fc2e5cf74184e579caea1282b3be74f:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="cd49a9b597394132b30313efd07dd9b1"><span offset-key="cd49a9b597394132b30313efd07dd9b1:0">This code displays a bullet list of numbers between 1 and 5.</span></span>

# 

<span key="f8a3a46b8025492e83d9108323ae6744"><span offset-key="f8a3a46b8025492e83d9108323ae6744:0">Basic List Component</span></span>

<span key="c7da5b85831b4f2aa569d02c95178269"><span offset-key="c7da5b85831b4f2aa569d02c95178269:0">Usually you would render lists inside a </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/components-and-props.html" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="43bffd7388774757882283a8e7a1f9f3" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="26d8dbc3c976423ebede3b1467a41d3b"><span data-offset-key="26d8dbc3c976423ebede3b1467a41d3b:0">component</span></span></span></a><span key="e58889694fe24ded8aa23b9abdd530e2"><span offset-key="e58889694fe24ded8aa23b9abdd530e2:0">.</span></span>

<span key="75d28aa3eb1e4a1394de464645d75eb9"><span offset-key="75d28aa3eb1e4a1394de464645d75eb9:0">We can refactor the previous example into a component that accepts an array of numbers and outputs a list of elements.</span></span>

<span key="f35adb439281497788c51f3d397120ad"><span offset-key="f35adb439281497788c51f3d397120ad:0">When you run this code, you'll be given a warning that a key should be provided for list items. A "key" is a special string attribute you need to include when creating lists of elements. We'll discuss why it's important in the next section.</span></span>

<span key="204fa6a3ddf4494485a52d8d34f5d2cb"><span offset-key="204fa6a3ddf4494485a52d8d34f5d2cb:0">Let's assign a key to our list items inside numbers.map() and fix the missing key issue.</span></span>

<span key="b6c73bfbc2754908a49aa1662f5e387d"><span offset-key="b6c73bfbc2754908a49aa1662f5e387d:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/jrXYRR?editors=0011" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="60a3754a7f10493d8e5a2f4ab73c0415" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="873effaa67e24f25ba1dbbff64bbbbc1"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="d9168ff28f384ef19e4653918ef70fd0"><span offset-key="d9168ff28f384ef19e4653918ef70fd0:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

# 

<span key="69c2a7e478c54fb392f4b6138a8488ea"><span offset-key="69c2a7e478c54fb392f4b6138a8488ea:0">Keys</span></span>

<span key="1e09c5bccb534e1a88ae3d94232dce93"><span offset-key="1e09c5bccb534e1a88ae3d94232dce93:0">Keys help React identify which items have changed, are added, or are removed. Keys should be given to the elements inside the array to give the elements a stable identity:</span></span>

<span key="824762444b7e489dbf5c83937a4c921d"><span offset-key="824762444b7e489dbf5c83937a4c921d:0">The best way to pick a key is to use a string that uniquely identifies a list item among its siblings. Most often you would use IDs from your data as keys:</span></span>

<span key="26c68265744042a9921c2a6c1dab407c"><span offset-key="26c68265744042a9921c2a6c1dab407c:0">When you don't have stable IDs for rendered items, you may use the item index as a key as a last resort:</span></span>

<span key="24bb7b0a332543ac955b66d546b0e7aa"><span offset-key="24bb7b0a332543ac955b66d546b0e7aa:0">We don't recommend using indexes for keys if the order of items may change. This can negatively impact performance and may cause issues with component state. Check out Robin Pokorny's article for an </span></span><a href="https://medium.com/@robinpokorny/index-as-a-key-is-an-anti-pattern-e0349aece318" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="c1e591ef18c549bb9ff1f0a7587dea42" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="14d760dbd1aa48d29cbc1929018f2d41"><span data-offset-key="14d760dbd1aa48d29cbc1929018f2d41:0">in-depth explanation on the negative impacts of using an index as a key</span></span></span></a><span key="8ea48926a9da468b84942a205a3ba2ac"><span offset-key="8ea48926a9da468b84942a205a3ba2ac:0">. If you choose not to assign an explicit key to list items then React will default to using indexes as keys.</span></span>

<span key="18bd4a7941374e3faf23c7c2ddcee8de"><span offset-key="18bd4a7941374e3faf23c7c2ddcee8de:0">Here is an </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/reconciliation.html#recursing-on-children" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="067fd559d3b84c9cb844e47753f85ba6" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="2f3155bf01ab4cc7859c852d2b29d195"><span data-offset-key="2f3155bf01ab4cc7859c852d2b29d195:0">in-depth explanation about why keys are necessary</span></span></span></a><span key="11d3a541d2494d7c900b0244f1165b30"><span offset-key="11d3a541d2494d7c900b0244f1165b30:0"> if you're interested in learning more.</span></span>

# 

<span key="bd6e34e5e9564a3ea80bd43e633112eb"><span offset-key="bd6e34e5e9564a3ea80bd43e633112eb:0">Extracting Components with Keys</span></span>

<span key="2181611c72a04c8d8c3162fd503c790f"><span offset-key="2181611c72a04c8d8c3162fd503c790f:0">Keys only make sense in the context of the surrounding array.</span></span>

<span key="f4c7d863ffcf4eeda7200d44b4e234f0"><span offset-key="f4c7d863ffcf4eeda7200d44b4e234f0:0">For example, if you </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/components-and-props.html#extracting-components" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="c8ef59abce9e46dd802ca8360bddf4cb" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="a7fe3a79eac942219609f963cd13ea29"><span data-offset-key="a7fe3a79eac942219609f963cd13ea29:0">extract</span></span></span></a><span key="94c195ef9aa546328ae0901d8f64dac4"><span offset-key="94c195ef9aa546328ae0901d8f64dac4:0"> a ListItem component, you should keep the key on the &lt;ListItem /> elements in the array rather than on the &lt;li> element in the ListItem itself.</span></span>

<span key="acb34edfcf6a462a8196dfbc9c3bcd8a">**Example: Incorrect Key Usage**</span>

<span key="6512d4d7f7334d85a4f706fb81ead0fc">**Example: Correct Key Usage**</span>

<span key="bd144bb2e51b45268cd7730bc724f073"><span offset-key="bd144bb2e51b45268cd7730bc724f073:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/ZXeOGM?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="becef99aeefd40f29b3eaecf83a718e4" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="a5f5fa31e92a4146ad1ef69843b3db6c"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="143b2b40ba064c5eac86ea2067f93f17"><span offset-key="143b2b40ba064c5eac86ea2067f93f17:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="29c6b2dca6e5476cbf480fbbda9b0fd3"><span offset-key="29c6b2dca6e5476cbf480fbbda9b0fd3:0">A good rule of thumb is that elements inside the map() call need keys.</span></span>

# 

<span key="8c133e6ffe4a4213b372c8fbb4d9f6ca"><span offset-key="8c133e6ffe4a4213b372c8fbb4d9f6ca:0">Keys Must Only Be Unique Among Siblings</span></span>

<span key="a963f234fea2485f8360cef4c052a651"><span offset-key="a963f234fea2485f8360cef4c052a651:0">Keys used within arrays should be unique among their siblings. However, they don't need to be globally unique. We can use the same keys when we produce two different arrays:</span></span>

<span key="695cfc04bf3b4ff793cb0ad81971c461"><span offset-key="695cfc04bf3b4ff793cb0ad81971c461:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/NRZYGN?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="2d0ad782b3cd4d4bac6e93db4f345406" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="602afde660f64f2287c90f9c7b3d32c4"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="91b38f5dc52046b5bacf478bdf6c013c"><span offset-key="91b38f5dc52046b5bacf478bdf6c013c:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="d98ad2c8bcf0479b8e68dc9506f7f7ea"><span offset-key="d98ad2c8bcf0479b8e68dc9506f7f7ea:0">Keys serve as a hint to React but they don't get passed to your components. If you need the same value in your component, pass it explicitly as a prop with a different name:</span></span>

<span key="6572fb7483d447289be5575f3f52305d"><span offset-key="6572fb7483d447289be5575f3f52305d:0">With the example above, the Post component can read props.id, but not props.key.</span></span>

# 

<span key="ad9d032771774dde9346c4a878c70934"><span offset-key="ad9d032771774dde9346c4a878c70934:0">Embedding map() in JSX</span></span>

<span key="21f4f104b73c4076aab330e46cabdcf5"><span offset-key="21f4f104b73c4076aab330e46cabdcf5:0">In the examples above we declared a separate listItems variable and included it in JSX:</span></span>

<span key="92e6d577bec046d08bb36eafe1521008"><span offset-key="92e6d577bec046d08bb36eafe1521008:0">JSX allows </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/introducing-jsx.html#embedding-expressions-in-jsx" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="9cc529afef22412c8344ce877e5b40f7" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="872c7508bc8f4a49a341c15f212ecb6b"><span data-offset-key="872c7508bc8f4a49a341c15f212ecb6b:0">embedding any expression</span></span></span></a><span key="31a1842f16584c8aa663669892e1b838"><span offset-key="31a1842f16584c8aa663669892e1b838:0"> in curly braces so we could inline the map() result:</span></span>

<span key="78895569c97c4d0ab451e0ac6076e0c9"><span offset-key="78895569c97c4d0ab451e0ac6076e0c9:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/BLvYrB?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="853adbcf76f1468c86472fb4c94afdee" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="c9f5a6572cbd444cbb06bd40c07543e7"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="da9c6b14d1ce4f2fbc2c6818f7206f34"><span offset-key="da9c6b14d1ce4f2fbc2c6818f7206f34:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="1f98ae47d9ef4a12b044dfee699fd8b6"><span offset-key="1f98ae47d9ef4a12b044dfee699fd8b6:0">Sometimes this results in clearer code, but this style can also be abused. Like in JavaScript, it is up to you to decide whether it is worth extracting a variable for readability. Keep in mind that if the map() body is too nested, it might be a good time to </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/components-and-props.html#extracting-components" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="f8fca991304b4a2aa00710bd95040a56" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="2fb5a6735f5a431489af35b081d3f057"><span data-offset-key="2fb5a6735f5a431489af35b081d3f057:0">extract a component</span></span></span></a><span key="fcacde705fd645c4897d0bbbc0715c4e"><span offset-key="fcacde705fd645c4897d0bbbc0715c4e:0">.</span></span>

# 

<span key="d1470564ccbc40dfae6d7e9d8635e64c">**Forms**</span>

# 

<span key="83cd6fd09b934b0dbc28c1f17dbd9595"><span offset-key="83cd6fd09b934b0dbc28c1f17dbd9595:0">HTML form elements work a bit differently from other DOM elements in React, because form elements naturally keep some internal state. For example, this form in plain HTML accepts a single name:</span></span>

<span key="fbaac7ca4ccd4a47b5a1b01a43cfc8c7"><span offset-key="fbaac7ca4ccd4a47b5a1b01a43cfc8c7:0">This form has the default HTML form behavior of browsing to a new page when the user submits the form. If you want this behavior in React, it just works. But in most cases, it's convenient to have a JavaScript function that handles the submission of the form and has access to the data that the user entered into the form. The standard way to achieve this is with a technique called "controlled components".</span></span>

# 

<span key="d7ca989647d445a1ae2a8f59d1067cc3"><span offset-key="d7ca989647d445a1ae2a8f59d1067cc3:0">Controlled Components</span></span>

<span key="d9f971891da441f19a6a7ee2b62ad32a"><span offset-key="d9f971891da441f19a6a7ee2b62ad32a:0">In HTML, form elements such as &lt;input>, &lt;textarea>, and &lt;select> typically maintain their own state and update it based on user input. In React, mutable state is typically kept in the state property of components, and only updated with \[setState()\](&lt;</span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/react-component.html#setstate%3E" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="c0d03114f12d41cbb6233c7f5f2144e3" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="a711529bab1f479d99df4b69de2f5310"><span data-offset-key="a711529bab1f479d99df4b69de2f5310:0">https://reactjs.org/docs/react-component.html#setstate&gt;</span></span></span></a><span key="7cd70d1bcf944d089725c16c616fe489"><span offset-key="7cd70d1bcf944d089725c16c616fe489:0">).</span></span>

<span key="d061f01d0fe14d42bd327192a6792349"><span offset-key="d061f01d0fe14d42bd327192a6792349:0">We can combine the two by making the React state be the "single source of truth". Then the React component that renders a form also controls what happens in that form on subsequent user input. An input form element whose value is controlled by React in this way is called a "controlled component".</span></span>

<span key="0607286ca690489fa19eb1bddc202838"><span offset-key="0607286ca690489fa19eb1bddc202838:0">For example, if we want to make the previous example log the name when it is submitted, we can write the form as a controlled component:</span></span>

<span key="223e0a95a9ad4c2981d5caef5346c407"><span offset-key="223e0a95a9ad4c2981d5caef5346c407:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/VmmPgp?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="f07c0e994bed417d990b551cb0e2e8c0" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="6f3f287ae560498da9a82b20e8871bff"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="89dd45ad71904e06afe5395d3f9e890d"><span offset-key="89dd45ad71904e06afe5395d3f9e890d:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="7b3ad130476d438e8b8691fdc311555f"><span offset-key="7b3ad130476d438e8b8691fdc311555f:0">Since the value attribute is set on our form element, the displayed value will always be this.state.value, making the React state the source of truth. Since handleChange runs on every keystroke to update the React state, the displayed value will update as the user types.</span></span>

<span key="04ee93da28044380ae4e5d2ca17a174d"><span offset-key="04ee93da28044380ae4e5d2ca17a174d:0">With a controlled component, the input's value is always driven by the React state. While this means you have to type a bit more code, you can now pass the value to other UI elements too, or reset it from other event handlers.</span></span>

# 

<span key="5da99c1a0b2c4602b9d0fbc41ffcbd5f"><span offset-key="5da99c1a0b2c4602b9d0fbc41ffcbd5f:0">The textarea Tag</span></span>

<span key="b0ec4411934247108042737f64313cd7"><span offset-key="b0ec4411934247108042737f64313cd7:0">In HTML, a &lt;textarea> element defines its text by its children:</span></span>

<span key="cf543ee0989b47f48a07bae429fc0bc8"><span offset-key="cf543ee0989b47f48a07bae429fc0bc8:0">In React, a &lt;textarea> uses a value attribute instead. This way, a form using a &lt;textarea> can be written very similarly to a form that uses a single-line input:</span></span>

<span key="bbb3958b3794484991bb29a4b524b0d9"><span offset-key="bbb3958b3794484991bb29a4b524b0d9:0">Notice that this.state.value is initialized in the constructor, so that the text area starts off with some text in it.</span></span>

# 

<span key="9e1198d99b7547439e02454db34b2b27"><span offset-key="9e1198d99b7547439e02454db34b2b27:0">The select Tag</span></span>

<span key="557a98173b30450ebc55d267b9bf120c"><span offset-key="557a98173b30450ebc55d267b9bf120c:0">In HTML, &lt;select> creates a drop-down list. For example, this HTML creates a drop-down list of flavors:</span></span>

<span key="103f230763fa446ea99070b3b5b5747e"><span offset-key="103f230763fa446ea99070b3b5b5747e:0">&lt;select>&lt;option value="grapefruit">Grapefruit&lt;/option>&lt;option value="lime">Lime&lt;/option>&lt;option selected value="coconut">Coconut&lt;/option>&lt;option value="mango">Mango&lt;/option>&lt;/select></span></span>

<span key="8473daa673574b7e974b62cdb9721b37"><span offset-key="8473daa673574b7e974b62cdb9721b37:0">Note that the Coconut option is initially selected, because of the selected attribute. React, instead of using this selected attribute, uses a value attribute on the root select tag. This is more convenient in a controlled component because you only need to update it in one place. For example:</span></span>

<span key="d4641e4e3acc4929825db1e9a967c248"><span offset-key="d4641e4e3acc4929825db1e9a967c248:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/JbbEzX?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="ffe3a58439da474ca34bd8562eb46308" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="e5d8ae0d64884a60b8e8451b981e5140"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="5740ca1f9728484680337bcb06dc055e"><span offset-key="5740ca1f9728484680337bcb06dc055e:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="99e0d063074b49f19d63abdcfe90e061"><span offset-key="99e0d063074b49f19d63abdcfe90e061:0">Overall, this makes it so that &lt;input type="text">, &lt;textarea>, and &lt;select> all work very similarly - they all accept a value attribute that you can use to implement a controlled component.</span></span>

> <span key="ce15c9bf030c4799a32b447b194b6a11"><span offset-key="ce15c9bf030c4799a32b447b194b6a11:0">NoteYou can pass an array into the value attribute, allowing you to select multiple options in a select tag:&lt;select multiple={true} value={\['B', 'C'\]}></span></span>

# 

<span key="5ca4971aa18b40c8bf17fc9cc657980b"><span offset-key="5ca4971aa18b40c8bf17fc9cc657980b:0">The file input Tag</span></span>

<span key="f820f7f32209440086618967d3ae2a8b"><span offset-key="f820f7f32209440086618967d3ae2a8b:0">In HTML, an &lt;input type="file"> lets the user choose one or more files from their device storage to be uploaded to a server or manipulated by JavaScript via the </span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/File/Using_files_from_web_applications" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="95dfcb5382014a758cc39a8adfe2cbb0" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="9d16dbca18514941a8779cdb949bdd1c"><span data-offset-key="9d16dbca18514941a8779cdb949bdd1c:0">File API</span></span></span></a><span key="05605deefe694ba980c9af2affd15dbb"><span offset-key="05605deefe694ba980c9af2affd15dbb:0">.</span></span>

<span key="af6726d22d9942828a953e9b23d0ac91"><span offset-key="af6726d22d9942828a953e9b23d0ac91:0">&lt;input type="file" /></span></span>

<span key="1a14039703c3432594ad6acba45cdae9"><span offset-key="1a14039703c3432594ad6acba45cdae9:0">Because its value is read-only, it is an </span>**uncontrolled**<span offset-key="1a14039703c3432594ad6acba45cdae9:2"> component in React. It is discussed together with other uncontrolled components </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/uncontrolled-components.html#the-file-input-tag" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="f19990ee68614e7ca1a1511760f4d6c1" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="ba1bab6d09ee4065949f2a4ff1ef9c47"><span data-offset-key="ba1bab6d09ee4065949f2a4ff1ef9c47:0">later in the documentation</span></span></span></a><span key="92a7ea806a154a4ba6590e0ece160c3f"><span offset-key="92a7ea806a154a4ba6590e0ece160c3f:0">.</span></span>

# 

<span key="41807e0c4bd94fec8ab24ad455ea5c14"><span offset-key="41807e0c4bd94fec8ab24ad455ea5c14:0">Handling Multiple Inputs</span></span>

<span key="6ba0a39d74eb450c95fea45f8f92b2ea"><span offset-key="6ba0a39d74eb450c95fea45f8f92b2ea:0">When you need to handle multiple controlled input elements, you can add a name attribute to each element and let the handler function choose what to do based on the value of event.target.name.</span></span>

<span key="940351fade9c4d1f978716acaf41ef77"><span offset-key="940351fade9c4d1f978716acaf41ef77:0">For example:</span></span>

<span key="4202b2584d1342f18bc665fa0d8610fa"><span offset-key="4202b2584d1342f18bc665fa0d8610fa:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/wgedvV?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="fd69f1ba62e94947833c13957cb162b8" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="5881311084fe423b9a9f8f03842ab906"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="e9fdcabe6d024161bdd53a0fd3de5732"><span offset-key="e9fdcabe6d024161bdd53a0fd3de5732:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="822f7a9406ff4ee5b88beb6a4b6c32c5"><span offset-key="822f7a9406ff4ee5b88beb6a4b6c32c5:0">Note how we used the ES6 </span></span><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Operators/Object_initializer#Computed_property_names" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="6d02e1c3632d4566972829ff0c76e690" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="156b822095a748fcb68c1a02edca5c76"><span data-offset-key="156b822095a748fcb68c1a02edca5c76:0">computed property name</span></span></span></a><span key="194d8d4f8e5540ccbc4724b8bacbd136"><span offset-key="194d8d4f8e5540ccbc4724b8bacbd136:0"> syntax to update the state key corresponding to the given input name:</span></span>

<span key="a7423a1fdbc142dda52a60d9e5b8d651"><span offset-key="a7423a1fdbc142dda52a60d9e5b8d651:0">It is equivalent to this ES5 code:</span></span>

<span key="5fcddb274698435fa99db6884107ea58"><span offset-key="5fcddb274698435fa99db6884107ea58:0">Also, since setState() automatically </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/state-and-lifecycle.html#state-updates-are-merged" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="698d740a859f46a5bba1946a40864290" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="eae9d63a852e4278abce063e872eb581"><span data-offset-key="eae9d63a852e4278abce063e872eb581:0">merges a partial state into the current state</span></span></span></a><span key="35da3430454e40deb92f44f4f28d3dd2"><span offset-key="35da3430454e40deb92f44f4f28d3dd2:0">, we only needed to call it with the changed parts.</span></span>

# 

<span key="d9cf0e220b8f4a5aa4f8785fe74a0fc5"><span offset-key="d9cf0e220b8f4a5aa4f8785fe74a0fc5:0">Controlled Input Null Value</span></span>

<span key="b41f7f355e6e4a67bcdd35e291214a35"><span offset-key="b41f7f355e6e4a67bcdd35e291214a35:0">Specifying the value prop on a </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/forms.html#controlled-components" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="baf975041cd34b7abcf59f40dbc5167e" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="e089bda48be04eaa8a80803a7f17f528"><span data-offset-key="e089bda48be04eaa8a80803a7f17f528:0">controlled component</span></span></span></a><span key="9904d4fccd8f4842a0c61819dfb388f1"><span offset-key="9904d4fccd8f4842a0c61819dfb388f1:0"> prevents the user from changing the input unless you desire so. If you've specified a value but the input is still editable, you may have accidentally set value to undefined or null.</span></span>

<span key="552042d0f9a44322a0d739e0078e8c06"><span offset-key="552042d0f9a44322a0d739e0078e8c06:0">The following code demonstrates this. (The input is locked at first but becomes editable after a short delay.)</span></span>

# 

<span key="cfe8d25e78cf4124b6218e1d638dccf1"><span offset-key="cfe8d25e78cf4124b6218e1d638dccf1:0">Alternatives to Controlled Components</span></span>

<span key="20bf844a98f74bcd87b0e9f618a86609"><span offset-key="20bf844a98f74bcd87b0e9f618a86609:0">It can sometimes be tedious to use controlled components, because you need to write an event handler for every way your data can change and pipe all of the input state through a React component. This can become particularly annoying when you are converting a preexisting codebase to React, or integrating a React application with a non-React library. In these situations, you might want to check out </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/uncontrolled-components.html" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="df3ae86e52334ea3946b60689d72dfe3" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="aa5c06eb3e8949f59cbbb76a6ee66c60"><span data-offset-key="aa5c06eb3e8949f59cbbb76a6ee66c60:0">uncontrolled components</span></span></span></a><span key="aa61914d64c64ee1a139a94405f37bfd"><span offset-key="aa61914d64c64ee1a139a94405f37bfd:0">, an alternative technique for implementing input forms.</span></span>

# 

<span key="40d3448e7e7d4eb5a512d1b895b2e5aa"><span offset-key="40d3448e7e7d4eb5a512d1b895b2e5aa:0">Fully-Fledged Solutions</span></span>

<span key="c9c4b804196c425d963a7c3efb44306b"><span offset-key="c9c4b804196c425d963a7c3efb44306b:0">If you're looking for a complete solution including validation, keeping track of the visited fields, and handling form submission, </span></span><a href="https://jaredpalmer.com/formik" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="a280d2c7db334222bf5201e6519ea9de" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="e658b75e3c7c4999a28c6c3e6988fc66"><span data-offset-key="e658b75e3c7c4999a28c6c3e6988fc66:0">Formik</span></span></span></a><span key="0ff674ee919d4a3f8ba6ada692749e13"><span offset-key="0ff674ee919d4a3f8ba6ada692749e13:0"> is one of the popular choices. However, it is built on the same principles of controlled components and managing state --- so don't neglect to learn them.</span></span>

# 

<span key="08df6d33adcf416496aa67f8eea394ac">**Lifting State Up**</span>

# 

<span key="450e5e53706c4eb8b5d1ac863ff7efd2"><span offset-key="450e5e53706c4eb8b5d1ac863ff7efd2:0">Often, several components need to reflect the same changing data. We recommend lifting the shared state up to their closest common ancestor. Let's see how this works in action.</span></span>

<span key="a259e187e1ee481f97137146b2bb49b3"><span offset-key="a259e187e1ee481f97137146b2bb49b3:0">In this section, we will create a temperature calculator that calculates whether the water would boil at a given temperature.</span></span>

<span key="b4df934bcdd0427ba6a9270e47c6c496"><span offset-key="b4df934bcdd0427ba6a9270e47c6c496:0">We will start with a component called BoilingVerdict. It accepts the celsius temperature as a prop, and prints whether it is enough to boil the water:</span></span>

<span key="84914bf905b04d908d572dca9ceaacd4"><span offset-key="84914bf905b04d908d572dca9ceaacd4:0">Next, we will create a component called Calculator. It renders an &lt;input> that lets you enter the temperature, and keeps its value in this.state.temperature.</span></span>

<span key="32efb2479f5b4836b0c8723b98d7b3eb"><span offset-key="32efb2479f5b4836b0c8723b98d7b3eb:0">Additionally, it renders the BoilingVerdict for the current input value.</span></span>

<span key="3e6504d263c9444f9ff01a25539475f7"><span offset-key="3e6504d263c9444f9ff01a25539475f7:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/ZXeOBm?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="ed535acc508c43c78b8a7e84782ad919" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="8b3d2ced748c4fbab7bb7b41475e3220"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="dd9faaa8c4d14bc1b346036009ad505e"><span offset-key="dd9faaa8c4d14bc1b346036009ad505e:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

# 

<span key="37e5a77a783145789277b47887e0b280"><span offset-key="37e5a77a783145789277b47887e0b280:0">Adding a Second Input</span></span>

<span key="96d48b3ac54d46c38eacb09710aa8850"><span offset-key="96d48b3ac54d46c38eacb09710aa8850:0">Our new requirement is that, in addition to a Celsius input, we provide a Fahrenheit input, and they are kept in sync.</span></span>

<span key="32e41f38c03343219ddb2bca27cf8b9c"><span offset-key="32e41f38c03343219ddb2bca27cf8b9c:0">We can start by extracting a TemperatureInput component from Calculator. We will add a new scale prop to it that can either be "c" or "f":</span></span>

<span key="57a2f9bf82094da0ac90b2ecbb833158"><span offset-key="57a2f9bf82094da0ac90b2ecbb833158:0">We can now change the Calculator to render two separate temperature inputs:</span></span>

<span key="126feb2d2bf849fdac6dcff7e063575e"><span offset-key="126feb2d2bf849fdac6dcff7e063575e:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/jGBryx?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="9c5d690907bf467d9c686b0bf9ce12cb" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="62639217b00948e5a0c4a02c7b4bde7a"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="eca11daa34274aa09e130903153d85fd"><span offset-key="eca11daa34274aa09e130903153d85fd:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="d2b8d1e8d9e24d28b899365ad6017727"><span offset-key="d2b8d1e8d9e24d28b899365ad6017727:0">We have two inputs now, but when you enter the temperature in one of them, the other doesn't update. This contradicts our requirement: we want to keep them in sync.</span></span>

<span key="a1f7b8913c034918b9635312c04575d2"><span offset-key="a1f7b8913c034918b9635312c04575d2:0">We also can't display the BoilingVerdict from Calculator. The Calculator doesn't know the current temperature because it is hidden inside the TemperatureInput.</span></span>

# 

<span key="d9ba37e451d0420790a6a081e2270eee"><span offset-key="d9ba37e451d0420790a6a081e2270eee:0">Writing Conversion Functions</span></span>

<span key="532ce2483b5344b399bd43ca57279de2"><span offset-key="532ce2483b5344b399bd43ca57279de2:0">First, we will write two functions to convert from Celsius to Fahrenheit and back:</span></span>

<span key="e968cb22c2044e77a460bfd1e7fbf3f1"><span offset-key="e968cb22c2044e77a460bfd1e7fbf3f1:0">These two functions convert numbers. We will write another function that takes a string temperature and a converter function as arguments and returns a string. We will use it to calculate the value of one input based on the other input.</span></span>

<span key="310f3586dc894736953c01a32dd4d0b1"><span offset-key="310f3586dc894736953c01a32dd4d0b1:0">It returns an empty string on an invalid temperature, and it keeps the output rounded to the third decimal place:</span></span>

<span key="533cb144c6be4d269e72277ead39dca8"><span offset-key="533cb144c6be4d269e72277ead39dca8:0">For example, tryConvert('abc', toCelsius) returns an empty string, and tryConvert('10.22', toFahrenheit) returns '50.396'.</span></span>

# 

<span key="61ce7123e93d4da1a241899d03da846b"><span offset-key="61ce7123e93d4da1a241899d03da846b:0">Lifting State Up</span></span>

<span key="2f634dfa76cf40c9ac3d873034306881"><span offset-key="2f634dfa76cf40c9ac3d873034306881:0">Currently, both TemperatureInput components independently keep their values in the local state:</span></span>

<span key="9f6bbaae96104f4cbaef20c234a05e7b"><span offset-key="9f6bbaae96104f4cbaef20c234a05e7b:0">However, we want these two inputs to be in sync with each other. When we update the Celsius input, the Fahrenheit input should reflect the converted temperature, and vice versa.</span></span>

<span key="9727e3f4894b4acf95934f34853e8ea5"><span offset-key="9727e3f4894b4acf95934f34853e8ea5:0">In React, sharing state is accomplished by moving it up to the closest common ancestor of the components that need it. This is called "lifting state up". We will remove the local state from the TemperatureInput and move it into the Calculator instead.</span></span>

<span key="e1f0ea71e070454aa2ff3b558e53ddb0"><span offset-key="e1f0ea71e070454aa2ff3b558e53ddb0:0">If the Calculator owns the shared state, it becomes the "source of truth" for the current temperature in both inputs. It can instruct them both to have values that are consistent with each other. Since the props of both TemperatureInput components are coming from the same parent Calculator component, the two inputs will always be in sync.</span></span>

<span key="7de0fa51e19e4eb4b0a799df1634d8a0"><span offset-key="7de0fa51e19e4eb4b0a799df1634d8a0:0">Let's see how this works step by step.</span></span>

<span key="858af2bf5b1c4dbfac9829dcc64d9044"><span offset-key="858af2bf5b1c4dbfac9829dcc64d9044:0">First, we will replace this.state.temperature with this.props.temperature in the TemperatureInput component. For now, let's pretend this.props.temperature already exists, although we will need to pass it from the Calculator in the future:</span></span>

<span key="1e812853f6374fbb901c6b73f234a576"><span offset-key="1e812853f6374fbb901c6b73f234a576:0">We know that </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/components-and-props.html#props-are-read-only" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="bef0f73aae3d482e8a9f4f091c18c639" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="aa582155a041452ebff16231bdde2661"><span data-offset-key="aa582155a041452ebff16231bdde2661:0">props are read-only</span></span></span></a><span key="e57f2bc2f60e4a08b69500230439d712"><span offset-key="e57f2bc2f60e4a08b69500230439d712:0">. When the temperature was in the local state, the TemperatureInput could just call this.setState() to change it. However, now that the temperature is coming from the parent as a prop, the TemperatureInput has no control over it.</span></span>

<span key="2b5865e1f5114e33af505150ed72a500"><span offset-key="2b5865e1f5114e33af505150ed72a500:0">In React, this is usually solved by making a component "controlled". Just like the DOM &lt;input> accepts both a value and an onChange prop, so can the custom TemperatureInput accept both temperature and onTemperatureChange props from its parent Calculator.</span></span>

<span key="48aa1246827b4dd0842d82937a56dd27"><span offset-key="48aa1246827b4dd0842d82937a56dd27:0">Now, when the TemperatureInput wants to update its temperature, it calls this.props.onTemperatureChange:</span></span>

> <span key="05d48db2e063463f8f30b92e706cde20"><span offset-key="05d48db2e063463f8f30b92e706cde20:0">Note:There is no special meaning to either temperature or onTemperatureChange prop names in custom components. We could have called them anything else, like name them value and onChange which is a common convention.</span></span>

<span key="399fe347296d4d4a813bf51a41c071b2"><span offset-key="399fe347296d4d4a813bf51a41c071b2:0">The onTemperatureChange prop will be provided together with the temperature prop by the parent Calculator component. It will handle the change by modifying its own local state, thus re-rendering both inputs with the new values. We will look at the new Calculator implementation very soon.</span></span>

<span key="f8c0d8ca012a45498a12d814f2d46998"><span offset-key="f8c0d8ca012a45498a12d814f2d46998:0">Before diving into the changes in the Calculator, let's recap our changes to the TemperatureInput component. We have removed the local state from it, and instead of reading this.state.temperature, we now read this.props.temperature. Instead of calling this.setState() when we want to make a change, we now call this.props.onTemperatureChange(), which will be provided by the Calculator:</span></span>

<span key="bf9d20f9cced40a48584aafc72df8432"><span offset-key="bf9d20f9cced40a48584aafc72df8432:0">Now let's turn to the Calculator component.</span></span>

<span key="c6e6ee1f20ea472d8695c23526b96adb"><span offset-key="c6e6ee1f20ea472d8695c23526b96adb:0">We will store the current input's temperature and scale in its local state. This is the state we "lifted up" from the inputs, and it will serve as the "source of truth" for both of them. It is the minimal representation of all the data we need to know in order to render both inputs.</span></span>

<span key="3f6bdde4221b4139b1691c75cf7bc7ea"><span offset-key="3f6bdde4221b4139b1691c75cf7bc7ea:0">For example, if we enter 37 into the Celsius input, the state of the Calculator component will be:</span></span>

<span key="4d831a3cca3a49feb951c93009bb8ebe"><span offset-key="4d831a3cca3a49feb951c93009bb8ebe:0">If we later edit the Fahrenheit field to be 212, the state of the Calculator will be:</span></span>

<span key="7ffd31adf4d14baaa08eb1780c4fb4d6"><span offset-key="7ffd31adf4d14baaa08eb1780c4fb4d6:0">We could have stored the value of both inputs but it turns out to be unnecessary. It is enough to store the value of the most recently changed input, and the scale that it represents. We can then infer the value of the other input based on the current temperature and scale alone.</span></span>

<span key="01ff73f07b15448187b17fca869176ed"><span offset-key="01ff73f07b15448187b17fca869176ed:0">The inputs stay in sync because their values are computed from the same state:</span></span>

<span key="12a0170079424ee5b537fbf529e591d3"><span offset-key="12a0170079424ee5b537fbf529e591d3:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span><a href="https://codepen.io/gaearon/embed/WZpxpz?editors=0010" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="c12ccf7429c94332988cc608b68fb509" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="debf5affa33549a18426811145c09f96"><strong>Try it on CodePen</strong></span></span></a><span key="a302c035dd774d00b17c58c000110ab2"><span offset-key="a302c035dd774d00b17c58c000110ab2:0"><span slate-zero-width="z">â€‹</span></span></span>

<span key="a7d29b98034f4802b88fc0182ee6a547"><span offset-key="a7d29b98034f4802b88fc0182ee6a547:0">Now, no matter which input you edit, this.state.temperature and this.state.scale in the Calculator get updated. One of the inputs gets the value as is, so any user input is preserved, and the other input value is always recalculated based on it.</span></span>

<span key="2e73e60f1cf74736b63b953230f8ab85"><span offset-key="2e73e60f1cf74736b63b953230f8ab85:0">Let's recap what happens when you edit an input:</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSIgc3R5bGU9ImhlaWdodDoxMnB4O3ZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm" />

    <span key="f4bd77b7d6b94cd6a715986f91ab383f"><span offset-key="f4bd77b7d6b94cd6a715986f91ab383f:0">React calls the function specified as onChange on the DOM &lt;input>. In our case, this is the handleChange method in the TemperatureInput component.</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSIgc3R5bGU9ImhlaWdodDoxMnB4O3ZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm" />

    <span key="133cd33f399d4712a835729e56742557"><span offset-key="133cd33f399d4712a835729e56742557:0">The handleChange method in the TemperatureInput component calls this.props.onTemperatureChange() with the new desired value. Its props, including onTemperatureChange, were provided by its parent component, the Calculator.</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSIgc3R5bGU9ImhlaWdodDoxMnB4O3ZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm" />

    <span key="4355d1d51aed4600a441878913a3e162"><span offset-key="4355d1d51aed4600a441878913a3e162:0">When it previously rendered, the Calculator had specified that onTemperatureChange of the Celsius TemperatureInput is the Calculator's handleCelsiusChange method, and onTemperatureChange of the Fahrenheit TemperatureInput is the Calculator's handleFahrenheitChange method. So either of these two Calculator methods gets called depending on which input we edited.</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSIgc3R5bGU9ImhlaWdodDoxMnB4O3ZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm" />

    <span key="e2d9b4388f084ad583f0f9788c653e65"><span offset-key="e2d9b4388f084ad583f0f9788c653e65:0">Inside these methods, the Calculator component asks React to re-render itself by calling this.setState() with the new input value and the current scale of the input we just edited.</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSIgc3R5bGU9ImhlaWdodDoxMnB4O3ZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm" />

    <span key="e02ec3992c5a4cdfb55bc8e56d112df3"><span offset-key="e02ec3992c5a4cdfb55bc8e56d112df3:0">React calls the Calculator component's render method to learn what the UI should look like. The values of both inputs are recomputed based on the current temperature and the active scale. The temperature conversion is performed here.</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSIgc3R5bGU9ImhlaWdodDoxMnB4O3ZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm" />

    <span key="e0a4c0e021314034a1e3c24a3ca23762"><span offset-key="e0a4c0e021314034a1e3c24a3ca23762:0">React calls the render methods of the individual TemperatureInput components with their new props specified by the Calculator. It learns what their UI should look like.</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSIgc3R5bGU9ImhlaWdodDoxMnB4O3ZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm" />

    <span key="cc0d11cdd5574b62860e6c49195378e6"><span offset-key="cc0d11cdd5574b62860e6c49195378e6:0">React calls the render method of the BoilingVerdict component, passing the temperature in Celsius as its props.</span></span>

-   <img src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgOCAxNiIgcHJlc2VydmVhc3BlY3RyYXRpbz0ieE1pZFlNaWQgbWVldCIgY2xhc3M9InItMW5mNGpibSIgc3R5bGU9ImhlaWdodDoxMnB4O3ZlcnRpY2FsLWFsaWduOm1pZGRsZTt3aWR0aDoxMnB4Ij48cGF0aCBkPSJNMCA4YzAtMi4yIDEuOC00IDQtNHM0IDEuOCA0IDQtMS44IDQtNCA0LTQtMS44LTQtNHoiIGZpbGw9ImN1cnJlbnRDb2xvciIgZmlsbC1ydWxlPSJldmVub2RkIj48L3BhdGg+PC9zdmc+" class="r-1nf4jbm" />

    <span key="03b483222a5c42f0a284237606616a6a"><span offset-key="03b483222a5c42f0a284237606616a6a:0">React DOM updates the DOM with the boiling verdict and to match the desired input values. The input we just edited receives its current value, and the other input is updated to the temperature after conversion.</span></span>

<span key="22fe2c60ba61483ebb3005cd1a37c381"><span offset-key="22fe2c60ba61483ebb3005cd1a37c381:0">Every update goes through the same steps so the inputs stay in sync.</span></span>

# 

<span key="ba527f5b378742c19f2173f18913780d"><span offset-key="ba527f5b378742c19f2173f18913780d:0">Lessons Learned</span></span>

<span key="59f1fd326b024188a4e3f5765b82c600"><span offset-key="59f1fd326b024188a4e3f5765b82c600:0">There should be a single "source of truth" for any data that changes in a React application. Usually, the state is first added to the component that needs it for rendering. Then, if other components also need it, you can lift it up to their closest common ancestor. Instead of trying to sync the state between different components, you should rely on the </span></span><a href="https://reactjs.org/docs/state-and-lifecycle.html#the-data-flows-down" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="3558b4072d85447ea493819d9062afd5" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="1b45d5c624334850b355d1c8471134f4"><span data-offset-key="1b45d5c624334850b355d1c8471134f4:0">top-down data flow</span></span></span></a><span key="33a3142b142248e68c2da09a78d75b35"><span offset-key="33a3142b142248e68c2da09a78d75b35:0">.</span></span>

<span key="2dbae269c5ef43fab96f61f9707a177c"><span offset-key="2dbae269c5ef43fab96f61f9707a177c:0">Lifting state involves writing more "boilerplate" code than two-way binding approaches, but as a benefit, it takes less work to find and isolate bugs. Since any state "lives" in some component and that component alone can change it, the surface area for bugs is greatly reduced. Additionally, you can implement any custom logic to reject or transform user input.</span></span>

<span key="00376afa732949e78a3a9c951c15654e"><span offset-key="00376afa732949e78a3a9c951c15654e:0">If something can be derived from either props or state, it probably shouldn't be in the state. For example, instead of storing both celsiusValue and fahrenheitValue, we store just the last edited temperature and its scale. The value of the other input can always be calculated from them in the render() method. This lets us clear or apply rounding to the other field without losing any precision in the user input.</span></span>

<span key="aa16c393dc9441f596ac326aee233a40"><span offset-key="aa16c393dc9441f596ac326aee233a40:0">When you see something wrong in the UI, you can use </span></span><a href="https://github.com/facebook/react/tree/main/packages/react-devtools" class="css-4rbku5 css-1dbjc4n r-1loqt21 r-1471scf r-1otgn73 r-1i6wzkk r-lrvibr"><span data-key="4598e02b7de847878c189a1b7f30e748" data-rnw-int-class="nearest_257-93055_259-93056-237__"><span data-key="610cb30afef74b90843f5003b364944a"><span data-offset-key="610cb30afef74b90843f5003b364944a:0">React Developer Tools</span></span></span></a><span key="af299532169149d4aba272893fc57dde"><span offset-key="af299532169149d4aba272893fc57dde:0"> to inspect the props and move up the tree until you find the component responsible for updating the state. This lets you trace the bugs to their source:</span></span>

# 

<span key="49de7d46223d44ba9259554a481f7353">**Composition vs Inheritance**</span>

# 

<span key="5cfb28462213437a9df59c4f4b043277"><span offset-key="5cfb28462213437a9df59c4f4b043277:0">React has a powerful composition model, and we recommend using composition instead of inheritance to reuse code between components.</span></span>

<span key="ab3fee8341ed4a148f5058c9e8298bce"><span offset-key="ab3fee8341ed4a148f5058c9e8298bce:0">In this section, we will consider a few problems where developers new to React often reach for inheritance, and show how we can solve them with composition.</span></span>

# 

<span key="a69af7ae0439417e945d6f6941563b08"><span offset-key="a69af7ae0439417e945d6f6941563b08:0">Containment</span></span>

<span key="2c46a8f955954a38b78038206bac2aed"><span offset-key="2c46a8f955954a38b78038206bac2aed:0">Some components don't know their children ahead of time. This is especially common for components like Sidebar or Dialog that represent generic "boxes".</span></span>

<span key="d9d7fa41826846428370aac69df6f064"><span offset-key="d9d7fa41826846428370aac69df6f064:0">We recommend that such components use the special children prop to pass children elements directly into their output:</span></span>

<span key="4c63b51c94964ddeb3a4818346168f0e"><span offset-key="4c63b51c94964ddeb3a4818346168f0e:0">This lets other components pass arbitrary children to them by nesting the JSX:</span></span>
